Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Testimony of a Slave After Emancipation and Proof of Freedom
Ruling on acceptance of testimony from a freed slave and burden of proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for accepting the testimony of an emancipated slave and identify who bears the burden of proof when a witness's status is challenged.

Core Idea
A freed slave's testimony is accepted only if the emancipation is effective; burden of proof shifts based on the claim.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies two important points about witness qualification in Hanafi law: first, the emancipation that qualifies a former slave to testify must be effective (nafidha) and not suspended; second, the burden of proof for challenging a witness's freedom or integrity lies on the party making the claim. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly assessing witness admissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct issues
The passage addresses (1) when a slave's testimony after emancipation is valid, and (2) who bears the burden of proof when a witness's status is challenged.
Separate the issues.
2
Isolate the condition for testimony after emancipation
The author emphasizes that the emancipation must be 'effective' (nafidha) and not suspended (mu'allaqa). The example from al-Bazzaziyya illustrates a suspended case: emancipation during death-illness when the slave is the only asset.
Effective emancipation means the slave is fully free without any contingency.
3
Determine the burden of proof in two scenarios
If the defendant claims the witnesses are slaves, the plaintiff must prove their freedom. If the defendant claims they were flogged for qadhf, the defendant must prove that.
The default is presumption of freedom and justice.
4
Understand the practical implications
The distinction affects how litigants prepare evidence. The plaintiff must have proof of freedom ready if the defendant attacks the witnesses' status; the defendant must have proof if he brings a specific disqualification like qadhf.
The ruling protects the default integrity of witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فشمل ما إذا تحملها لمولاه ثم أداها بعد عتقه كما في فتح القدير. وأراد بالحرية الحرية النافذة، وإنما قيدنا به لما في البزازية أعتق عبده في مرض موته ولا مال له غيره ثم شهد هذا لا تقبل عند الإمام لأن عتقه موقوف ا هـ . وفي السراجية : إذا طعن المدعى عليه في الشهود أنهم عبيد فعلى المدعي إقامة البينة على حريتهم ولو قال هما محدودان في القذف فعلى الطاعن إقامة البينة
Thus it includes [the case] where [the slave] bore the testimony for his master and then performed it after his emancipation, as in Fath al-Qadir. And by 'freedom' he meant the effective freedom. We only qualified with that because in al-Bazzaziyya: if someone emancipates his slave in his death-sickness and he has no other property, then [the slave] testifies, it is not accepted according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] because his emancipation is suspended. And in al-Sirajiyya: If the defendant impugns the witnesses [saying] that they are slaves, then upon the claimant is the burden to establish their freedom. And if he says they are two who have been flogged for qadhf, then upon the impugner is the burden to establish [that they have been flogged].
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage addresses two related issues concerning the acceptance of testimony based on the witness's status of freedom. First, for a slave's testimony to be accepted after emancipation, the emancipation must be effective (nāfidha) and not suspended or revocable. The commentator clarifies a historical point from the Bazzaziyya: if a master in his death-illness emancipates a slave when he has no other property, the emancipation is suspended (because it is considered a bequest from one-third of the estate) and thus the slave's testimony during that period is not accepted according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Second, the burden of proof regarding the status of witnesses is discussed: if the defendant claims the witnesses are slaves, the plaintiff must prove their freedom. Conversely, if the defendant claims the witnesses have been flogged for qadhf, he must prove that fact. This distinction arises because the default presumption for a witness is freedom and integrity ('adala). The passage does not explicitly cite a Quranic or hadith proof but relies on the established principles of the madhhab.

Key Terms
الحرية النافذة (al-hurriyya al-nafidha): Effective freedom that is complete and not suspended
المحدود في القذف (al-mahdud fi al-qadhf): A person who has received the hadd punishment for false accusation of adultery

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a case where a slave bore testimony for his master while a slave, then the master emancipated him with an effective emancipation (nafidha), is his testimony accepted?
A) Yes, unconditionally
B) Yes, because the emancipation is effective and the testimony is now given after freedom
C) No, because the testimony was initiated while a slave
D) Only if the emancipation was witnessed by two just witnesses

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a freed slave's testimony hinges on the emancipation being effective, not merely any emancipation; and the burden of proof for witness disqualification lies with the party that asserts the disqualifying fact.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
14 min
The Permanent Rejection of Testimony of One Flogged for Qadhf: Proofs and Exceptions
Extensive discussion of the ruling that the testimony of one flogged for false accusation is permanently rejected, with proofs, exceptions, and inter-madhhab debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a person flogged for qadhf, explain the Quranic proof and the inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i, and identify the exception for bringing four witnesses.

Core Idea
The testimony of a qadhif is permanently rejected even after repentance because the hadd creates a permanent preventative.

This lesson examines a ruling that seems harsh at first glance: even sincere repentance does not restore the right to testify for one who has been flogged for false accusation of adultery. But the ruling is grounded in a direct Quranic command and a deep understanding of the nature of hadd punishments. We will unpack the evidence, the reasoning behind the Hanafi position, and the critical difference of opinion with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Subject
Read the core statement: 'And the one flogged for qadhf, even if he repents, his testimony is not accepted.' Note that the ruling applies to someone who has actually been flogged completely, not to one who merely committed the act but was not punished.
The condition of having been flogged distinguishes this from mere fisq.
2
Locate the Primary Proof
Find the Quranic citation: Surah al-Nur:4 – 'And never accept their testimony.' Identify the phrase and note that it is a prohibition (nahy), which in Hanafi usul indicates invalidity.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala according to Hanafis.
3
Analyze the Reasoning: Why Permanence?
The commentary explains that the rejection is 'part of the hadd being a preventative.' This means the hadd itself creates a bar (man') that outlasts the punishment. Unlike other sins where rejection is due to fisq (removed by repentance), here the rejection is structural.
Contrast with flogging for other sins: there the rejection is fisq-based, so repentance removes it.
4
Examine the Exception Clause and the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
The verse continues 'except those who repent.' The Hanafis argue this exception applies only to the description 'fasiqun', not to the prohibition. The Shafi'is disagree, applying the exception to the whole verse. Understand the evidence each side uses and the practical consequence.
The key is where the pronoun 'lahum' refers: to the flogged (Hanafi) or to the accusers unable to prove (Shafi'i).
5
Note the Exception: Bringing Four Witnesses
There is one way the testimony can be restored: if the flogged person himself brings four witnesses proving that the accused actually committed zina. This nullifies the basis of the original hadd.
This applies even if the four witnesses come after the flogging, because the new evidence shows the accusation was true.

Source Text

قوله : (والمحدود في قذف ولو (تاب لا تقبل شهادته لقوله تعالى ولا تقبلوا لهم شهادة أبدا [النور: ٤] ولأنه من تمام الحد لكونه مانعاً فيبقى بعد التوبة كأصله بخلاف المحدود في غيره لأن الرد للفسق وقد ارتفع بالتوبة والاستثناء في الآية ينصرف إلى ما يليه وهو قوله تعالى وأولئك هم الفاسقون﴾ [النور: ٤] أو هو استثناء منقطع بمعنى لكن؛ كذا في الهداية. وفي التحرير الأوجه أنه متصل، وقرره في التلويح بأن المعنى أولئك الذين يرمون المحصنات محكوم عليهم بالفسق إلا التائبين، وأما رجوع الاستثناء إلى الكل في آية المحاربين فلدليل اقتضاه وهو قوله من قبل أن تقدروا عليهم﴾ [المائدة: ٣٤] فإنه لو عاد إلى الأخير أعني قوله لهم عذاب عظيم لم يبق له فائدة لأن التوبة تسقطه مطلقاً ففائدته سقوط الحد وتمامه في فتح القدير وفي البدائع : كل فاسق تاب عن فسقه قبلت توبته وشهادته إلا اثنين : المحدود في القذف والمعروف بالكذب، لأن من صار معروفاً بالكذب واشتهر به لا يعرف صدقه من توبته بخلاف الفاسق إذا تاب عن سائر أنواع الفسق فإن شهادته تقبل ا هـ . وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله إلى أن شهادته لا تسقط ما لم يضرب تمام الحد وهو صريح المبسوط لأن المحدود من ضرب الحد أي تماماً لأن ما دونه يكون تعزيراً غير مسقط لها. ولو قال المؤلف إن لم يقم بينة على صدقه لكان أولى لأنه لو أقام أربعة بعد ما حد على زنی قبلت شهادته بعد التوبة في الصحيح لأنه لو أقامها قبله لم يحد فكذا لا ترد شهادته ؛ كذا ذكر الشارح وتمامه في العتابية وإنما قيد بقوله على أنه زنى لأنه لو أقام بينة على إقرار المقذوف بالزنا لا يشترط أن يكونوا أربعة لما في فتح القدير من باب حد القذف؛ فإن شهد رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان على إقرار المقذوف بالزنا يدرأ الحد عن القاذف لأن الثابت بالبينة كالثابت بالمعاينة إلى آخره فكذا إذا أقام رجلين بعد حده على إقراره بالزنا تعود شهادته كما لا يخفى . ثم اعلم أن الضمير في قوله « لهم عندنا عائد إلى المحدودين، وعند الشافعي إلى القاذفين العاجزين عن الإثبات كما ذكره الفخر الرازي فلو لم يحد تقبل شهادته عندنا خلافاً له، ولو قذف رجلاً ثم شهد مع ثلاثة على أنه زنى فإذا كان حد لم يحد المشهود عليه وإن لم يحد القاذف حد المشهود عليه ؛ كذا في البزازية . قوله : (إلا أن يحد الكافر في قذف ثم أسلم يعني فتقبل ولو كان محدوداً في قذف لأن للكافر شهادة فكان ردها من تمام الحد وبالإسلام حدثت شهادة أخرى، وليس المراد أنها تقبل بعد إسلامه في حق المسلمين فقط . قال المؤلف في الكافي : فإن أسلم قبلت شهادته عليهم وعلى المسلمين ضرورة وتمامه في العتابية قيد بالكافر لأن العبد إذا حد حد القذف ثم عتق حيث ترد شهادته لأنه لا شهادة للعبد أصلاً في حال رقه فيتوقف الرد على حدوثها فإذا حدث كان رد شهادته بعد العتق من تمام حده، وظاهر كلام المؤلف أنه أسلم بعد ما ضرب تمام الحد فلو أسلم بعد ما ضرب بعضه فضرب الباقي بعد إسلامه ففيه ثلاث روايات في ظاهر الرواية لا تبطل شهادته على التأبيد فإذا تاب ،قبلت وفي رواية تبطل إن ضرب الأكثر بعد إسلامه، وفي رواية ولو سوطاً ؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج ووضع هذه المسألة يدل على أن الإسلام لا يسقط حد القذف. وهل يسقط شيئاً من الحدود؟ قال الشيخ عمر قارئ الهداية : إذا سرق الذمي أو زنى ثم أسلم فإن ثبت عليه ذلك بإقراره أو بشهادة المسلمين لا يدرأ عنه، وإن ثبت بشهادة أهل الذمة فأسلم سقط عنه الحد ا هـ . وينبغي أن يقال كذلك في حد القذف. وفي اليتيمة من كتاب السير : إن الذمي إذا وجب التعزير عليه فأسلم لم يسقط ولم أر حكم الصبي إذا وجب التعزير عليه للتأديب فبلغ ونقل الفخر الرازي عن الشافعية سقوطه لزجره بالبلوغ ومقتضى ما في اليتيمة أنه لا يسقط إلا أن يوجد نقل صريح
His statement: (And the one flogged for qadhf, even if he repents, his testimony is not accepted) due to Allah's statement: 'And never accept their testimony' (Surah al-Nur:4). And because it is part of the hadd being a preventative, so it remains after repentance as originally. Unlike one flogged for other [sins] because the rejection is due to fisq and that is removed by repentance. And the exception in the verse refers to what follows it, i.e., His statement 'and those are the transgressors' (Surah al-Nur:4), or it is a disconnected exception meaning 'but'. Thus in al-Hidaya. And in al-Tahrir, the more likely is that it is connected, and he established in al-Talwih that the meaning is: those who accuse chaste women are judged as transgressors except those who repent. As for the return of the exception to all in the verse of the highwaymen (Surah al-Ma'ida:34), it is due to an evidence that requires it, which is His statement 'before you have power over them'. For if it returned to the last, i.e., His statement 'for them a great punishment', there would be no benefit, because repentance removes it absolutely, so its benefit is dropping the hadd. The full discussion is in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Bada'i': Every transgressor who repents from his transgression, his repentance and testimony are accepted, except two: the one flogged for qadhf and the one known for lying, because one who becomes known for lying and is famous for it, his truthfulness cannot be known from his repentance, unlike the transgressor who repents from other types of transgression, for his testimony is accepted. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) indicated that his testimony is not dropped unless the full hadd has been inflicted, and this is explicit in al-Mabsut, because 'the one flogged' is one who has been struck the hadd fully, for less than that is ta'zir and does not drop it. If the author had said 'unless he brings proof of his truthfulness', it would have been better, because if he brings four witnesses after being flogged for zina, his testimony is accepted after repentance according to the correct view, because if he had brought them before, he would not have been flogged, so likewise his testimony is not rejected. Thus the commentator mentioned, and the full discussion is in al-Atabiyya. He only restricted by saying 'for zina' because if he brings proof of the accused's admission of zina, it is not required that they be four, as in Fath al-Qadir from the chapter of hadd qadhf: if two men or one man and two women testify to the accused's admission of zina, the hadd is averted from the accuser, because what is established by proof is like what is established by eyewitness. So also if he brings two men after his flogging on his admission of zina, his testimony is restored. Then know that the pronoun 'them' in His statement 'for them' according to us refers to the flogged [qadhifun], and according to al-Shafi'i to the accusers who are unable to prove [their claim], as al-Fakhr al-Razi mentioned. So if he has not been flogged, his testimony is accepted according to us, contrary to him. And if a person accuses a man then testifies with three [others] that he committed zina, then if the accused is flogged, the one who accused is not flogged, and if the accuser is not flogged, the accused is flogged. Thus in al-Bazzaziyya. His statement: (Unless a disbeliever is flogged for qadhf then becomes Muslim) means his testimony is accepted, even if he was flogged for qadhf, because a disbeliever has testimony, so its rejection was part of the hadd, and with Islam another testimony begins. It is not meant that it is accepted after his Islam only with respect to Muslims. The author said in al-Kafi: If he becomes Muslim, his testimony is accepted against them and against Muslims by necessity. The full discussion is in al-Atabiyya. He restricted to the disbeliever because if a slave is flogged with the hadd of qadhf then emancipated, his testimony is rejected, because a slave has no testimony at all during his servitude, so the rejection depends on it occurring. When it occurs, the rejection of his testimony after emancipation is part of his hadd. The apparent meaning of the author's statement is that he became Muslim after the full hadd was inflicted. If he became Muslim after part of it was inflicted and the rest was inflicted after his Islam, there are three narrations: in the apparent narration, his testimony is not permanently void, so if he repents it is accepted. In another narration, it becomes void if the majority was inflicted after his Islam. In another narration, even a whip. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The placement of this issue indicates that Islam does not nullify the hadd of qadhf. Does it nullify any of the hudud? Shaykh Umar Qari' al-Hidaya said: If a dhimmi steals or commits zina then becomes Muslim, if it is established against him by his confession or by the testimony of Muslims, it is not averted from him; if established by the testimony of ahl al-dhimma then he becomes Muslim, the hadd is dropped. It should be said likewise for hadd qadhf. And in al-Yatima from the book of Siyar: If a dhimmi incurs ta'zir then becomes Muslim, it is not dropped. And I have not seen the ruling for a minor who incurs ta'zir for discipline then becomes mature. Al-Fakhr al-Razi transmitted from the Shafi'is that it is dropped because he is restrained by puberty. The implication of what is in al-Yatima is that it is not dropped unless an explicit text is found.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a detailed commentary on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq that the testimony of a person who has been flogged for false accusation of adultery (qadhf) is never accepted, even after repentance. The commentary begins by citing the Quranic proof from Surah al-Nur verse 4: 'And never accept their testimony.' It then explains the reasoning: the rejection of testimony is part of the preventive effect of the hadd punishment, so it persists after repentance, unlike flogging for other sins where the rejection is due to fisq (transgression) which is removed by repentance. The passage then enters a discussion of the exception clause in the verse ('except those who repent'), analyzing whether it applies to the entire ruling or only to the description of the offenders as 'fasiqun'. The Hanafi position is that the exception is connected only to the word 'fasiqun', not to the prohibition of accepting testimony, relying on the context and on qiyas with the verse of highwaymen (Surah al-Ma'ida:34) where a specific evidence forces the exception to apply to all parts. From al-Bada'i', it is stated that normally repentance restores testimony for all sins except two: qadhf and habitual lying, because a habitual liar's truthfulness cannot be known. The commentary further explains that the full hadd must be inflicted; if only part is inflicted, it is considered ta'zir and does not permanently reject testimony. An important exception is mentioned: if the flogged person brings four witnesses to prove that the accused actually committed zina, then his testimony is accepted after repentance, because the original flogging was based on a false accusation that has now been countered. The inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i is then detailed: the pronoun 'lahum' in the verse is interpreted by the Hanafis as referring to the flogged accusers (the ones who have been flogged), whereas al-Shafi'i interprets it as referring to the accusers who failed to produce four witnesses. Practically, the Hanafi view is that the testimony of a qadhif is permanently rejected even after repentance, while the Shafi'i view is that repentance restores it. Next, the commentator addresses the case of a disbeliever (kafir) who is flogged for qadhf and then accepts Islam. According to the Hanafi school, his testimony is accepted after Islam, because the rejection was tied to his disbelief and the hadd; with Islam, a new testimony capacity arises. This is contrasted with a slave who is flogged and then emancipated: the slave's testimony remains rejected because in his previous state of slavery he had no testimony at all, so the rejection becomes permanent. Finally, the passage discusses the effect of Islam on hadd punishments: does Islam nullify a hadd? It mentions three narrations regarding a person who converts to Islam after being partially flogged: in the apparent narration, his testimony is not permanently void after repentance; in another, it is void if the majority of the flogging occurred after Islam; in a third, even a single stripe. This shows that Islam does not nullify the hadd of qadhf, but may affect its completion. The passage concludes with a quote from Shaykh Umar Qari' al-Hidaya about the effect of Islam on other hudud for dhimmis, and an analogy to hadd qadhf, along with a note on ta'zir.

Key Terms
المحدود في القذف (al-mahdud fi al-qadhf): A person who has received the hadd punishment (flogging) for the crime of falsely accusing a married person of adultery (qadhf).
التوبة (al-tawba): Repentance from sin, which normally removes the legal disqualification of fisq (transgression) for testimony, but not for the hadd of qadhf.
الحد (al-hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by the Quran or Sunnah, such as flogging for qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is flogged for falsely accusing Zayd of zina. After repenting, can his testimony ever be accepted according to the Hanafi school?
A) No, never under any circumstances
B) Yes, if he brings four witnesses that Zayd committed zina
C) Yes, after three years of good behavior
D) Only if he becomes a Muslim

Key Takeaway
The testimony of a person flogged for qadhf is permanently rejected in the Hanafi school, even after repentance, due to the Quranic imperative and the nature of the hadd as a permanent preventative (man'), except when the flogged person brings four witnesses proving the truth of his accusation.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
6 min
Ruling on Testimony Between Direct Lineal Relatives
Ruling statement with commentary expansion: testimony between branch and root is rejected.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony between ascendants and descendants and explain the rationale for its rejection.

Core Idea
Testimony between direct lineal ascendants and descendants is rejected categorically due to the strong suspicion of bias.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi testimony law: a person cannot testify for their parent, grandparent, child, or grandchild. The passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the testimony of the 'branch' (far') for the 'root' (asl) and vice versa is not accepted. This principle is based on the natural inclination that may compromise the witness's objectivity, making the testimony unreliable regardless of the witness's apparent trustworthiness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Determine who is the 'far'' (descendant) and who is the 'asl' (ascendant) in a given scenario. For example, a son is the far' of his father, and a mother is the asl of her daughter.
This classification includes all direct lineal relations: parents, grandparents, children, grandchildren.
2
State the ruling
Apply the ruling: testimony from a far' for an asl and from an asl for a far' is rejected (batil). This covers all such reciprocal relationships.
The ruling is absolute; it does not depend on the witness's trustworthiness or specific circumstances.
3
Understand the rationale
The rejection is based on the prevailing suspicion (tuhmah) of bias due to natural affection. The Hanafi school deems this suspicion so strong that it cannot be overcome by any claim of honesty.
Other schools may accept such testimony if the witness is known to be trustworthy, but Hanafi holds the categorical view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والولد) لأبويه وجديه وعكسه) أي لم تقبل شهادة الفرع لأصله والأصل لفرعه عنه .
His statement: (And the child) for his parents and grandparents and vice versa, meaning the testimony of the branch for the root and the root for the branch is not accepted.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This concise passage from the commentary explains the ruling on testimonies between close relatives. The witness is disqualified if the testimony is for a direct ascendant or descendant. This includes a child testifying for a parent or grandparent, and a parent or grandparent testifying for a child or grandchild. The reason is the strong natural inclination that may lead to bias, undermining the reliability of the testimony. This ruling applies to all such lineal relationships. The passage also implies the same for spouses and for a master and his slave, as mentioned earlier in the matn text that was quoted. The commentator confirms the general principle of reciprocal disqualification.

Key Terms
الفرع (al-far'): Descendant, i.e., child, grandchild, etc.
الأصل (al-asl): Ascendant, i.e., parent, grandparent, etc.
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Suspicion or presumption of bias, which is the reason for disqualification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A father testifies in favor of his son in a property dispute. According to the Hanafi school, is this testimony accepted?
A) Yes, because a father knows best
B) No, because testimony between ascendant and descendant is rejected
C) Yes, if the father is known to be trustworthy
D) Only if the son is a minor

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, testimony between a descendant and an ascendant is rejected due to the inherent suspicion of bias, and this rule applies reciprocally.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Acceptance of Testimony After Hadd for Qadhf
Explains ruling on testimony acceptance after hadd for qadhf with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the testimony of a person punished for qadhf is rejected only when the full hadd is executed, and identify the conditions under which it becomes acceptable again.

Core Idea
The rejection of testimony after hadd is a punishment — only applies when fully executed, removable by repentance and proof.

The testimony of a person who falsely accuses another of zina and receives the prescribed hadd is not automatically invalid forever. The Hanafi school holds that such rejection is contingent upon the full execution of the hadd, and after genuine repentance, if the person can produce four witnesses to the original zina or the accused confesses, his testimony becomes acceptable. This lesson unpacks the ruling with its proofs, examines the inter-madhhab difference with al-Shafi'i, and explores special scenarios involving disbelievers and slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qadhf (false accusation of zina) which incurs hadd. The ruling is about the testimony of the person who has been hadded. According to the text, his testimony is not accepted unless the full hadd is executed. If the hadd is not fully carried out, his testimony remains acceptable.
The rejection is tied to the punishment itself.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the Quranic verse (Surah al-Nur 24:4) which states: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses – lash them with eighty lashes and do not accept their testimony ever after.' The Hanafi school interprets 'their testimony' as referring to those who have been lashed (the hadded persons).
The verse explicitly mentions the hadd and the rejection of testimony together.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'do not accept their testimony ever after' follows immediately after the command to lash, indicating that the rejection is a consequence of the hadd. Therefore, if the hadd is not fully executed, the rejection does not apply. The Hanafi rule: the rejection is a punishment, so it only applies when the punishment is fully carried out.
This reasoning is based on the structure of the verse.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Shafi'i interprets the pronoun 'their testimony' as referring to the accusers (al-qadhifoon) who are unable to produce four witnesses, not specifically those who are hadded. Hence, Shafi'is reject the testimony of any false accuser regardless of whether they received the hadd.
This leads to different practical outcomes.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that the rejection is a punishment; it only applies when the hadd is fully executed. After repentance and if the person can produce four witnesses or the accused confesses, his testimony becomes acceptable again. The mufta bihi is that the testimony is accepted after repentance and evidence, as per the correct view (sahih) and zahir al-riwaya.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a qadhif who is not hadded can testify in Hanafi law, not in Shafi'i.

كتاب الشهادات باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل والولد لأبويه وجديه وعكسه وأحد الزوجين للآخر والسيد لعبده ومكاتبه والشريك أنه واشتهر به لا يعرف صدقه من توبته بخلاف الفاسق إذا تاب عن سائر أنواع الفسق فإن شهادته تقبل ا هـ . وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله إلى أن شهادته لا تسقط ما لم يضرب تمام الحد وهو صريح المبسوط لأن المحدود من ضرب الحد أي تماماً لأن ما دونه يكون تعزيراً غير مسقط لها. ولو قال المؤلف إن لم يقم بينة على صدقه لكان أولى لأنه لو أقام أربعة بعد ما حد على زنی قبلت شهادته بعد التوبة في الصحيح لأنه لو أقامها قبله لم يحد فكذا لا ترد شهادته ؛ كذا ذكر الشارح وتمامه في العتابية وإنما قيد بقوله على أنه زنى لأنه لو أقام بينة على إقرار المقذوف بالزنا لا يشترط أن يكونوا أربعة لما في فتح القدير من باب حد القذف؛ فإن شهد رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان على إقرار المقذوف بالزنا يدرأ الحد عن القاذف لأن الثابت بالبينة كالثابت بالمعاينة إلى آخره فكذا إذا أقام رجلين بعد حده على إقراره بالزنا تعود شهادته كما لا يخفى . ثم اعلم أن الضمير في قوله « لهم عندنا عائد إلى المحدودين، وعند الشافعي إلى القاذفين العاجزين عن الإثبات كما ذكره الفخر الرازي فلو لم يحد تقبل شهادته عندنا خلافاً له، ولو قذف رجلاً ثم شهد مع ثلاثة على أنه زنى فإذا كان حد لم يحد المشهود عليه وإن لم يحد القاذف حد المشهود عليه ؛ كذا في البزازية . قوله : (إلا أن يحد الكافر في قذف ثم أسلم يعني فتقبل ولو كان محدوداً في قذف لأن للكافر شهادة فكان ردها من تمام الحد وبالإسلام حدثت شهادة أخرى، وليس المراد أنها تقبل بعد إسلامه في حق المسلمين فقط . قال المؤلف في الكافي : فإن أسلم قبلت شهادته عليهم وعلى المسلمين ضرورة وتمامه في العتابية قيد بالكافر لأن العبد إذا حد حد القذف ثم عتق حيث ترد شهادته لأنه لا شهادة للعبد أصلاً في حال رقه فيتوقف الرد على حدوثها فإذا حدث كان رد شهادته بعد العتق من تمام حده، وظاهر كلام المؤلف أنه أسلم بعد ما ضرب تمام الحد فلو أسلم بعد ما ضرب بعضه فضرب الباقي بعد إسلامه ففيه ثلاث روايات في ظاهر الرواية لا تبطل شهادته على التأبيد فإذا تاب ،قبلت وفي رواية تبطل إن ضرب الأكثر بعد إسلامه، وفي رواية ولو سوطاً ؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج ووضع هذه المسألة يدل على أن الإسلام لا يسقط حد القذف. وهل يسقط شيئاً من الحدود؟ قال الشيخ عمر قارئ الهداية : إذا سرق الذمي أو زنى ثم أسلم فإن ثبت عليه ذلك بإقراره أو بشهادة المسلمين لا يدرأ عنه، وإن ثبت بشهادة أهل الذمة فأسلم سقط عنه الحد ا هـ . وينبغي أن يقال كذلك في حد القذف. وفي اليتيمة من كتاب السير : إن الذمي إذا وجب التعزير عليه فأسلم لم يسقط ولم أر حكم الصبي إذا وجب التعزير عليه للتأديب فبلغ ونقل الفخر الرازي عن الشافعية سقوطه لزجره بالبلوغ ومقتضى ما في اليتيمة أنه لا يسقط إلا أن يوجد نقل صريح
Chapter of testimonies, section: Whose testimony is accepted and whose is not. The child for his parents and grandparents and vice versa, and one of the two spouses for the other, and the master for his slave and his mukatab, and the partner. That he is known for it, his truthfulness is not known from his repentance, unlike the sinner when he repents from all other types of sin, then his testimony is accepted. And the author indicated that his testimony is not nullified as long as the full hadd is not struck. And if the author said 'if he does not establish proof of his truthfulness' it would be better, because if he brings four after being hadded for zina, his testimony is accepted after repentance according to the correct view. And if he brought them before, he would not be hadded, so likewise his testimony is not rejected. And he only specified 'that he committed zina' because if he brings evidence of the accused's confession to zina, it is not required that they be four. Then know that the pronoun 'them' for us refers to the hadded persons, and according to al-Shafi'i to the accusers unable to prove. So if he was not hadded, his testimony is accepted according to us, contrary to him. And if a man accuses a man then testifies with three that he committed zina, then if he is hadded, the one testified against is not hadded; if the accuser is not hadded, the one testified against is hadded. The saying: 'Unless the disbeliever is hadded for qadhf then accepts Islam' means it is accepted even if he was hadded for qadhf, because the disbeliever has testimony, so its rejection is part of the complete hadd, and with Islam another testimony arises. And it is not meant that it is accepted after his Islam only with respect to Muslims. The author said in al-Kafi: If he accepts Islam, his testimony is accepted against them and against Muslims necessarily. He restricted it to the disbeliever because the slave, when he is hadded for qadhf then emancipated, his testimony is thus rejected, because the slave has no testimony at all during his slavery, so the rejection depends on its occurrence. So when it occurs, the rejection of his testimony after emancipation is part of his complete hadd. The apparent meaning of the author is that he accepted Islam after the full hadd was struck. So if he accepted Islam after some of it was struck and the remainder was struck after his Islam, there are three narrations: in the apparent narration, his testimony is not invalidated forever, so when he repents it is accepted; in one narration it is invalidated if the majority is struck after his Islam; in one narration even if one lash. And this issue indicates that Islam does not nullify the hadd for qadhf. And does it nullify anything of the hudud? Shaykh Umar Qari al-Hidaya said: If a dhimmi steals or commits zina then accepts Islam, if that is established against him by his confession or by the testimony of Muslims, it is not warded off; if established by the testimony of dhimmis and he accepts Islam, the hadd drops from him. It should be said likewise for hadd qadhf. And in al-Yatimah from the book of Siyar: If a dhimmi is liable for ta'zir and then accepts Islam, it does not drop. And I have not seen the ruling of a minor if ta'zir is due on him for discipline and then he attains puberty. Fakhr al-Razi transmitted from the Shafi'is that it drops due to his deterrence by puberty, and the implication of what is in al-Yatimah is that it does not drop unless an explicit transmission exists.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by listing categories of people whose testimony is not accepted, as per the matn: child for parents and grandparents, spouses for each other, master for slave and mukatab, and partner. The commentary then focuses on the specific case of a person who has been punished (hadd) for qadhf (false accusation of zina). The key point is that the rejection of his testimony is contingent upon the full execution of the hadd; if the hadd is not fully carried out, his testimony is not rejected. After repentance, if he can produce four witnesses to the original zina (before he was hadded), his testimony becomes acceptable again. The text also explores a difference with al-Shafi'i regarding the pronoun reference in the Quranic verse (Surah al-Nur 24:4): for Hanafis, the verse refers to those punished for qadhf, while for Shafi'is it refers to the accusers who cannot produce four witnesses. Consequently, if the accuser was not hadded, his testimony is accepted in the Hanafi school, unlike Shafi'i. The passage then discusses special cases: a disbeliever who is hadded for qadhf and then accepts Islam — his testimony is accepted after Islam because Islam creates a new capacity for testimony. Similarly, a slave who is hadded and then freed: his testimony after freedom is rejected because the rejection was part of the hadd that occurred while he was a slave. If the hadd is partially executed before acceptance of Islam, there are three narrations within the Hanafi school regarding the validity of his testimony. The text concludes with a discussion of whether Islam drops hudud, quoting the view of Shaykh Umar Qari from al-Hidayah: for zina or theft, if the evidence is from Muslims, the hadd remains; if from dhimmis, the hadd drops upon Islam. The same applies to hadd for qadhf. Finally, it notes a difference with Shafi'is regarding ta'zir for a minor who reaches puberty — Hanafis hold that it does not drop unless explicit text exists.

Key Terms
القذف (al-qadhf): False accusation of zina (adultery/fornication) against a chaste person.
المحدود (al-mahdood): A person who has been legally hadded (punished with a fixed corporal penalty), specifically for qadhf.
التوبة (al-tawbah): Repentance from sin, which in this context allows the restoration of testimony acceptance after hadd, but only if accompanied by bringing evidence or a change in status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the testimony of a person who was hadded for qadhf accepted again?
A) Immediately after repentance without any evidence.
B) Only if he brings four witnesses to the original zina or the accused confesses.
C) After he pays a fine.
D) Never, even after repentance.

Key Takeaway
The rejection of testimony after hadd for qadhf is a punishment contingent on full execution of the hadd, and can be lifted by repentance and proof of the truth of the original accusation.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner

General Rule: Testimony Between Ascendants and Descendants
Ruling with proof and scope expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that testimony between ascendants and descendants is not accepted, identify the child of li'an as included, and explain the reasoning of connected benefits.

Core Idea
Testimony between parent and child is rejected because it is like testifying for oneself.

The Hanafi school holds that a descendant cannot testify for an ascendant, nor an ascendant for a descendant, due to a hadith and because their interests are intertwined. This prohibition extends to children established only in one respect, such as a child of li'an. In this lesson, we will analyze the rule and its rationale, including the scope of 'walad'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Locate the statement that testimony between ascendants and descendants is not accepted. Note the two proofs: a hadith and the connected benefits (munafa' muttasila).
The hadith is not quoted in this passage but is referenced.
2
Understand the scope of 'walad'
The term 'walad' is general and includes a child established in one respect only, such as a child of li'an. Recognize that the prohibition applies to all forms of filiation, even partial.
Partial filiation gives some rights (marriage prohibition, zakat restriction) but not inheritance or maintenance.
3
Apply to the child of li'an
State why the testimony of a child of li'an for his ascendants or for his descendant is not accepted: lineage is proven in one respect (from the father) but not from the accuser.
The child of li'an is like a child of fornication in this regard.
4
Identify the exception
Note that although the child of li'an is considered a child for testimony prohibition, inheritance and maintenance are not established between them.
This exception differentiates between various effects of filiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والولد) لأبويه وجديه وعكسه) أي لم تقبل شهادة الفرع لأصله والأصل لفرعه للحديث، ولأن المنافع بين الأولاد والآباء متصلة ولهذا لا يجوز أداء الزكاة إليهم فتكون شهادة لنفسه من وجه وأطلق الولد فشمل الولد من وجه فلا تقبل شهادة ولد الملاعن لأصوله أو هو له أو لفرعه لثبوته من وجه بدليل صحة دعوته منه وعدمها من غيره، وتحرم مناكحته ووضع الزكاة فيه فأحكام البنوة ثابتة له إلا الإرث والنفقة من الطرفين كولد العاهر. ولو باع أحد التوأمين وقد ولدا في ملكه وأعتقه المشتري فشهد البائعة تقبل؛ فإن ادعى الباقي ثبت نسبهما وانتقض البيع والعتق والقضاء ويرد ما قبض أو مثله إن هلك للاستناد لتحويل العقد، وإن كان القضاء قصاصاً في طرف أو نفس فأرشه عليه دون العاقلة وتمامه في تلخيص الجامع من باب شهادة ولد الملاعنة ولا تقبل شهادة ولد أم الولد المنفي من السيد ولا يعطيه الزكاة كولد الحرة المنفي باللعان؛ كذا في المحيط البرهاني. وفي فتح القدير : تجوز شهادته لابنه رضاعاً. وفي خزانة الأكمل : شهد ابناه أن الطالب أبرأ أباهما واحتال بدينه على فلان لم تجز إذا كان الطالب منكراً، وإن كان المال على غير أبيهما فشهدوا أن الطالب أحال به أباهما والطالب ينكر والمطلوب يدعي البراءة والحوالة جازت ا هـ. وفي المحيط البرهاني : إذا شهدا على فعل أبيهما فعلاً ملزماً لا تقبل إذا كان للأب فيه منفعة اتفاقاً وإلا فعلى قولهما لا تقبل وعن محمد روايتان. فلو قال إن كلمك فلان فأنت حر فادعى فلان أنه كلمه وشهد ابناه به لم تقبل عندهما، وكذا إذا علق عتقه بدخوله الدار، ولو أنكر الأب جازت شهادتهما. وكذا الحكم في كل شيء كان من فعل الأب من نكاح أو طلاق أو بيع، وإن شهد ابنا الوكيل على عقد الوكيل فهو على ثلاثة أوجه الأوّل أن يقر الموكل والوكيل بالأمر والعقد وهو على وجهين : فإن ادعاه الخصم قضى القاضي بالتصادق لا بالشهادة، وإن أنكر فعلى قولهما لا تقبل ولا يقضى بشيء إلا في الخلع فإنه يقضى بالطلاق بغير مال لإقرار الزوج به وهو الموكل. وعن محمد يقضى بالعقد إلا بعقد ترجع حقوقه إلى العاقد كالبيع. الثاني أن ينكر الوكيل والموكل فإن جحد الخصم لا تقبل وإلا تقبل اتفاقاً. الثالث أن يقر الوكيل بهما ويجحد الموكل العقد فقط فإن ادعاه الخصم يقضى بالعقود كلها إلا النكاح على قول أبي حنيفة وتمامه فيه . وقيد بالشهادة لهم لأن الشهادة على أصله وفرعه مقبولة إلا إذا شهد الجد على ابنه لابن ابنه قلنا إنها لا تقبل لوجود المانع من المشهود له. وفي المحيط قال محمد: رجل شهد لابن ابنه على أبيه تقبل لأنه حين شهد عليه لم يصر جداً لولده بل يصير جداً بعد حكم الحاكم بشهادته فحينئذ جداً يصير بموجب الشهادة والشيء لا ينفي موجب نفسه ا هـ . وهذا التعليل يفيد أن الكلام في شهادة الأب على إقرار ابنه بأن ما ولدته زوجته ابنه لا
His saying: (and the child) for his parents and grandparents and vice versa means the testimony of a descendant for his ascendant and the ascendant for his descendant is not accepted, due to the hadith, and because the benefits between children and parents are connected, and therefore paying zakat to them is not permissible, so it would be testimony for himself in a sense. And he used the general term 'child' which includes the child [established] in one respect, so the testimony of a child of a mula'an (husband who invoked li'an) for his ascendants or for him or for his descendant is not accepted, because he is [a child] in one respect, as evidenced by the validity of his claiming lineage from him and its invalidity from others, and marriage with him is prohibited, and placing zakat on him [is forbidden]. So the rulings of filiation are established for him except inheritance and maintenance from both sides, like the child of a fornicator. And if one of the twins is sold while they were born in his ownership, and the buyer emancipates him, then the seller testifies, it is accepted; but if the remaining one claims [lineage], both their lineages are established, and the sale and emancipation and judgment are rescinded, and he returns what he took or its like if it perished, due to the contract being overturned. And if the judgment was qisas on a limb or life, then the compensation is upon him, not on the 'aqila. The complete discussion is in Talkhis al-Jami' from the chapter on testimony of the child of a mula'anah. And the testimony of a child of an umm walad who is denied by the master is not accepted, nor is zakat given to him, like the child of a free woman denied by li'an; as in al-Muhit al-Burhani. In Fath al-Qadir: his testimony for his son by rada' is permissible. In Khizanat al-Akmal: His two sons testified that the claimant released their father from debt and transferred his debt to so-and-so, it is not allowed if the claimant denies; but if the debt was on someone other than their father and they testified that the claimant transferred it to their father, while the claimant denies and the defendant claims innocence and the transfer, it is allowed. In al-Muhit al-Burhani: If they testify concerning an act of their father that is binding, it is not accepted if the father has benefit in it by agreement; otherwise, according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] it is not accepted, and from Muhammad there are two narrations. So if he says, 'If so-and-so speaks to you, you are free,' then so-and-so claims he spoke to him, and his two sons testify to it, it is not accepted according to the two. Similarly, if he suspends his emancipation on his entering the house. And if the father denies, their testimony is accepted. The same ruling applies to everything that is an act of the father, such as marriage, divorce, or sale. And if the two sons of the agent testify concerning the agent's contract, it has three aspects. First, that the principal and the agent both affirm the matter and the contract; this has two aspects: if the opponent claims, the judge decides based on mutual confirmation, not testimony; if he denies, according to the two it is not accepted, and nothing is decided, except in khul' where divorce is decided without compensation due to the husband's admission. And from Muhammad: the contract is decided, except for a contract whose rights revert to the contracting party, like sale. Second, that the agent and the principal both deny; if the opponent denies, it is not accepted; otherwise, it is accepted by agreement. Third, that the agent affirms both and the principal denies only the contract; if the opponent claims, all contracts are decided except for marriage according to Abu Hanifa. And he restricted it to testimony for them because testimony against one's ascendant and descendant is accepted, except when the grandfather testifies against his son for his grandson: we say it is not accepted due to the impediment of the beneficiary. In al-Muhit, Muhammad said: A man testified for his grandson against his father; it is accepted, because when he testified against him, he was not a grandfather for his son; he becomes a grandfather only after the judge's ruling based on his testimony; then at that point he becomes a grandfather by virtue of the testimony, and a thing does not negate its own necessary consequence. This reasoning indicates that the discussion is about the testimony of a father concerning his son's admission that what his wife gave birth to is his son.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn's ruling that the testimony of a child for his parents and grandparents, and vice versa, is not accepted. The reason given is a hadith and the fact that mutual benefits are intertwined, making testimony akin to testifying for oneself. The definition of 'child' (walad) includes a child of li'an (mula'an) because he is considered a child in one respect (lineage is established only from the father, not from the accuser). Thus, his testimony for or against his ascendants is not accepted, except that inheritance and maintenance are not established between them. The text then explores various scenarios and exceptions. For example, the testimony of a father for his son against a claim of twin lineage is examined in a complex case involving sale and emancipation. It is accepted only if the remaining twin does not claim lineage. The testimony of a child of an umm walad (slave mother) who is denied by the master is not accepted, like the child of a free woman denied by li'an. However, there is an exception: testimony for a son by rada' (fosterage) is permitted. The passage then discusses at length the testimony of children regarding their father's actions or contracts, with differences between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. For instance, if a father makes a conditional emancipation dependent on someone speaking to him, and his sons testify that the condition occurred, their testimony is not accepted if the father might benefit. But if the father denies the condition, their testimony is accepted. The discussion extends to the testimony of the sons of an agent concerning the principal's contract, with three detailed scenarios. Finally, a special case is given: a grandfather testifying for his grandson (son's son) against his own son. According to Muhammad, this is accepted because at the time of testimony he is not yet a grandfather; he becomes a grandfather only after the testimony is accepted. Therefore, the impediment (being a grandfather as the beneficiary) does not exist when the testimony is given.

Key Terms
الولد (al-walad): Child, including the child of li'an and other types where lineage is established in one respect only.
الملاعن/الملاعنة (al-mula'an/al-mula'anah): A person who has invoked li'an (mutual imprecation) to deny paternity of a child. The child is attributed to the mother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the child of li'an included in the prohibition of testimony?
A) Because he is considered a full child for all purposes.
B) Because he is a child in one respect, enough to create connected benefits.
C) Because the hadith explicitly mentions him.
D) Because he can inherit from the father.

Key Takeaway
Testimony between ascendant and descendant is not accepted due to connected benefits, and this includes children with partial filiation like the child of li'an.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Exceptions and Special Cases: Twins, Umm Walad, and Rada'
Expansion and application of the rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of testimony between ascendants and descendants to complex scenarios involving twins born in one's ownership, children of umm walad, and foster children, and explain when testimony is accepted or rescinded.

Core Idea
Testimony may be accepted temporarily but rescinded if a hidden relationship is later established; foster sons are outside the prohibition.

While the general rule prohibits testimony between ascendants and descendants, the Hanafi school recognizes exceptions where the relationship is not fully established or where the testimony is not tainted by potential partiality. This lesson examines three such exceptions: the case of twins born in one's ownership, the child of a denied umm walad, and testimony for a son by rada' (fosterage). We will see how the ruling can be reversed if lineage is later proven.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the twin case
Read the scenario: one of two twins born in one's ownership is sold and then emancipated by the buyer. If the seller testifies (presumably about lineage), it is accepted. But if the remaining twin later claims lineage, the ruling is overturned.
The testimony is accepted only until the hidden relationship is exposed.
2
Identify the consequences of lineage establishment
If the remaining twin proves lineage, both sale and emancipation are rescinded, and the buyer must return the price or its equivalent. If the judgment involved qisas (retaliation), the compensation falls on the testifying party, not the 'aqila.
This emphasizes that testimony can have far-reaching effects when hidden relationships surface.
3
Understand the umm walad case
The testimony of a child of an umm walad (slave mother) who is denied by the master is not accepted, similar to the child of a free woman denied by li'an. Also, zakat cannot be given to such a child.
Denial severs some legal effects but not all; testimony remains invalid.
4
Recognize the exception for fosterage
Testimony for a son by rada' (fosterage) is permissible, as stated in Fath al-Qadir. This is because rada' creates a weaker bond than blood lineage.
This shows that the prohibition is not absolute; it applies only to blood relationships that involve connected benefits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والولد) لأبويه وجديه وعكسه) أي لم تقبل شهادة الفرع لأصله والأصل لفرعه للحديث، ولأن المنافع بين الأولاد والآباء متصلة ولهذا لا يجوز أداء الزكاة إليهم فتكون شهادة لنفسه من وجه وأطلق الولد فشمل الولد من وجه فلا تقبل شهادة ولد الملاعن لأصوله أو هو له أو لفرعه لثبوته من وجه بدليل صحة دعوته منه وعدمها من غيره، وتحرم مناكحته ووضع الزكاة فيه فأحكام البنوة ثابتة له إلا الإرث والنفقة من الطرفين كولد العاهر. ولو باع أحد التوأمين وقد ولدا في ملكه وأعتقه المشتري فشهد البائعة تقبل؛ فإن ادعى الباقي ثبت نسبهما وانتقض البيع والعتق والقضاء ويرد ما قبض أو مثله إن هلك للاستناد لتحويل العقد، وإن كان القضاء قصاصاً في طرف أو نفس فأرشه عليه دون العاقلة وتمامه في تلخيص الجامع من باب شهادة ولد الملاعنة ولا تقبل شهادة ولد أم الولد المنفي من السيد ولا يعطيه الزكاة كولد الحرة المنفي باللعان؛ كذا في المحيط البرهاني. وفي فتح القدير : تجوز شهادته لابنه رضاعاً. وفي خزانة الأكمل : شهد ابناه أن الطالب أبرأ أباهما واحتال بدينه على فلان لم تجز إذا كان الطالب منكراً، وإن كان المال على غير أبيهما فشهدوا أن الطالب أحال به أباهما والطالب ينكر والمطلوب يدعي البراءة والحوالة جازت ا هـ. وفي المحيط البرهاني : إذا شهدا على فعل أبيهما فعلاً ملزماً لا تقبل إذا كان للأب فيه منفعة اتفاقاً وإلا فعلى قولهما لا تقبل وعن محمد روايتان. فلو قال إن كلمك فلان فأنت حر فادعى فلان أنه كلمه وشهد ابناه به لم تقبل عندهما، وكذا إذا علق عتقه بدخوله الدار، ولو أنكر الأب جازت شهادتهما. وكذا الحكم في كل شيء كان من فعل الأب من نكاح أو طلاق أو بيع، وإن شهد ابنا الوكيل على عقد الوكيل فهو على ثلاثة أوجه الأوّل أن يقر الموكل والوكيل بالأمر والعقد وهو على وجهين : فإن ادعاه الخصم قضى القاضي بالتصادق لا بالشهادة، وإن أنكر فعلى قولهما لا تقبل ولا يقضى بشيء إلا في الخلع فإنه يقضى بالطلاق بغير مال لإقرار الزوج به وهو الموكل. وعن محمد يقضى بالعقد إلا بعقد ترجع حقوقه إلى العاقد كالبيع. الثاني أن ينكر الوكيل والموكل فإن جحد الخصم لا تقبل وإلا تقبل اتفاقاً. الثالث أن يقر الوكيل بهما ويجحد الموكل العقد فقط فإن ادعاه الخصم يقضى بالعقود كلها إلا النكاح على قول أبي حنيفة وتمامه فيه . وقيد بالشهادة لهم لأن الشهادة على أصله وفرعه مقبولة إلا إذا شهد الجد على ابنه لابن ابنه قلنا إنها لا تقبل لوجود المانع من المشهود له. وفي المحيط قال محمد: رجل شهد لابن ابنه على أبيه تقبل لأنه حين شهد عليه لم يصر جداً لولده بل يصير جداً بعد حكم الحاكم بشهادته فحينئذ جداً يصير بموجب الشهادة والشيء لا ينفي موجب نفسه ا هـ . وهذا التعليل يفيد أن الكلام في شهادة الأب على إقرار ابنه بأن ما ولدته زوجته ابنه لا
His saying: (and the child) for his parents and grandparents and vice versa means the testimony of a descendant for his ascendant and the ascendant for his descendant is not accepted, due to the hadith, and because the benefits between children and parents are connected, and therefore paying zakat to them is not permissible, so it would be testimony for himself in a sense. And he used the general term 'child' which includes the child [established] in one respect, so the testimony of a child of a mula'an (husband who invoked li'an) for his ascendants or for him or for his descendant is not accepted, because he is [a child] in one respect, as evidenced by the validity of his claiming lineage from him and its invalidity from others, and marriage with him is prohibited, and placing zakat on him [is forbidden]. So the rulings of filiation are established for him except inheritance and maintenance from both sides, like the child of a fornicator. And if one of the twins is sold while they were born in his ownership, and the buyer emancipates him, then the seller testifies, it is accepted; but if the remaining one claims [lineage], both their lineages are established, and the sale and emancipation and judgment are rescinded, and he returns what he took or its like if it perished, due to the contract being overturned. And if the judgment was qisas on a limb or life, then the compensation is upon him, not on the 'aqila. The complete discussion is in Talkhis al-Jami' from the chapter on testimony of the child of a mula'anah. And the testimony of a child of an umm walad who is denied by the master is not accepted, nor is zakat given to him, like the child of a free woman denied by li'an; as in al-Muhit al-Burhani. In Fath al-Qadir: his testimony for his son by rada' is permissible. In Khizanat al-Akmal: His two sons testified that the claimant released their father from debt and transferred his debt to so-and-so, it is not allowed if the claimant denies; but if the debt was on someone other than their father and they testified that the claimant transferred it to their father, while the claimant denies and the defendant claims innocence and the transfer, it is allowed. In al-Muhit al-Burhani: If they testify concerning an act of their father that is binding, it is not accepted if the father has benefit in it by agreement; otherwise, according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] it is not accepted, and from Muhammad there are two narrations. So if he says, 'If so-and-so speaks to you, you are free,' then so-and-so claims he spoke to him, and his two sons testify to it, it is not accepted according to the two. Similarly, if he suspends his emancipation on his entering the house. And if the father denies, their testimony is accepted. The same ruling applies to everything that is an act of the father, such as marriage, divorce, or sale. And if the two sons of the agent testify concerning the agent's contract, it has three aspects. First, that the principal and the agent both affirm the matter and the contract; this has two aspects: if the opponent claims, the judge decides based on mutual confirmation, not testimony; if he denies, according to the two it is not accepted, and nothing is decided, except in khul' where divorce is decided without compensation due to the husband's admission. And from Muhammad: the contract is decided, except for a contract whose rights revert to the contracting party, like sale. Second, that the agent and the principal both deny; if the opponent denies, it is not accepted; otherwise, it is accepted by agreement. Third, that the agent affirms both and the principal denies only the contract; if the opponent claims, all contracts are decided except for marriage according to Abu Hanifa. And he restricted it to testimony for them because testimony against one's ascendant and descendant is accepted, except when the grandfather testifies against his son for his grandson: we say it is not accepted due to the impediment of the beneficiary. In al-Muhit, Muhammad said: A man testified for his grandson against his father; it is accepted, because when he testified against him, he was not a grandfather for his son; he becomes a grandfather only after the judge's ruling based on his testimony; then at that point he becomes a grandfather by virtue of the testimony, and a thing does not negate its own necessary consequence. This reasoning indicates that the discussion is about the testimony of a father concerning his son's admission that what his wife gave birth to is his son.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn's ruling that the testimony of a child for his parents and grandparents, and vice versa, is not accepted. The reason given is a hadith and the fact that mutual benefits are intertwined, making testimony akin to testifying for oneself. The definition of 'child' (walad) includes a child of li'an (mula'an) because he is considered a child in one respect (lineage is established only from the father, not from the accuser). Thus, his testimony for or against his ascendants is not accepted, except that inheritance and maintenance are not established between them. The text then explores various scenarios and exceptions. For example, the testimony of a father for his son against a claim of twin lineage is examined in a complex case involving sale and emancipation. It is accepted only if the remaining twin does not claim lineage. The testimony of a child of an umm walad (slave mother) who is denied by the master is not accepted, like the child of a free woman denied by li'an. However, there is an exception: testimony for a son by rada' (fosterage) is permitted. The passage then discusses at length the testimony of children regarding their father's actions or contracts, with differences between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. For instance, if a father makes a conditional emancipation dependent on someone speaking to him, and his sons testify that the condition occurred, their testimony is not accepted if the father might benefit. But if the father denies the condition, their testimony is accepted. The discussion extends to the testimony of the sons of an agent concerning the principal's contract, with three detailed scenarios. Finally, a special case is given: a grandfather testifying for his grandson (son's son) against his own son. According to Muhammad, this is accepted because at the time of testimony he is not yet a grandfather; he becomes a grandfather only after the testimony is accepted. Therefore, the impediment (being a grandfather as the beneficiary) does not exist when the testimony is given.

Key Terms
التوأمين (al-taw'amayn): Twins. In the context, twins born in one's ownership (i.e., to a slave woman owned by the man).
أم الولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has given birth to her master's child; upon the master's death she becomes free.
الرضاع (al-rada'): Fosterage; a relationship created by breastfeeding, establishing certain prohibitions (marriage) but not inheritance or maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a remaining twin claims lineage after the seller has testified?
A) The testimony is upheld but the sale is rescinded.
B) The sale and emancipation are rescinded, and the buyer returns the price or its equivalent.
C) The testimony is rejected and the seller is punished.
D) The emancipation remains valid but the sale is void.

Key Takeaway
Testimony can be accepted conditionally and later rescinded if hidden lineage surfaces; foster sons are excluded from the prohibition.

Shahadat — Testimony
advanced
10 min
Testimony of Children on Father's Acts and Intra-Hanafi Differences
Intra-Hanafi dispute on a specific application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between cases where the testimony of children regarding their father's acts is accepted or rejected, and explain the differences between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on this issue.

Core Idea
Children's testimony on their father's acts is accepted only if the father denies having benefit; otherwise, it is rejected due to potential partiality.

A specific application of the general rule concerns children testifying about their father's actions, such as conditional emancipations or contracts. The Hanafi school splits on whether such testimony is admissible when the father may have a direct benefit. This lesson delves into the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, using the examples of conditional emancipation and the agent's contract.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general principle for father's acts
The passage states that if children testify about a binding act of their father, and the father has a benefit in it, the testimony is not accepted by agreement. If no benefit, the Sahibayn reject it, from Muhammad there are two narrations.
The key is whether the father benefits from the testimony being true.
2
Apply to conditional emancipation
If a father says, 'If so-and-so speaks to you, you are free,' and so-and-so claims he spoke, the children's testimony that he did is not accepted according to the Sahibayn. Similarly if emancipation is conditional on entering a house.
The father's benefit is that the slave remains free (to avoid liability or maintain status).
3
Note the exception when father denies
If the father himself denies that the condition occurred, then the children's testimony is accepted.
This shows that the father's own position matters.
4
Extend to other acts
The same ruling applies to marriage, divorce, sale, etc. The principle is general.
The 'illa is the potential benefit to the father.
5
Consider the agent's sons case
When the sons of an agent testify about the agent's contract, there are three scenarios depending on whether the principal and agent affirm or deny. Distinguish when the judge decides based on testimony or mutual acknowledgment.
This adds another layer of complexity involving multiple parties.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakil): Agent; one who is authorized to act on behalf of another (principal).
الموكل (al-muwakkil): Principal; the person who appoints an agent.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (or without, if the husband agrees).

According to the passage, when is the testimony of children regarding their father's act accepted by all Hanafi scholars?
A) When the father has no benefit in the act.
B) When the father denies that the act occurred.
C) When the act is a sale.
D) When the testimony is given in writing.

Key Takeaway
Children's testimony on father's acts is subject to intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf based on whether the father has benefit or denies the act.

Shahadat — Testimony
advanced

When a Grandfather Testifies for His Grandson Against His Son
Exception to the rule based on temporal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a grandfather's testimony for his grandson against his son, explain Muhammad's reasoning that the impediment arises only after the testimony, and contrast it with the general rule.

Core Idea
A grandfather can testify for his grandson because at the time of testimony, he is not yet a grandfather to that child—the relationship is created by the testimony itself.

A fascinating exception to the prohibition on ascendant-descendant testimony occurs when a grandfather testifies for his grandson against his own son. According to Muhammad, this is allowed because the testator is not yet a grandfather to the child; the very testimony establishes the grandson's lineage, making him a grandfather only after the fact. This reasoning shows the school's attention to the timing of relationships.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
The case is: a man testifies that a certain child is his son's son (i.e., his grandson). The son denies paternity. The grandfather's testimony is for the grandson against the son.
This is testimony for a descendant (grandson) against his own son (the descendant's father).
2
State Muhammad's ruling
Muhammad says the testimony is accepted. The reason: when he testified, he was not yet a grandfather to that child; he becomes a grandfather only after the judge accepts his testimony and establishes the lineage.
The impediment (being a grandfather with a benefit) does not exist at the time of testimony.
3
Analyze the reasoning ('illa)
The rule prohibits testimony when the testator is an ascendant of the beneficiary. Here, the grandfather becomes an ascendant only because of his own testimony. Muhammad argues that the cause of prohibition (being an ascendant) should not be created by the very act of testifying.
This is a subtle point: the testimony itself creates the relationship, so it cannot be rejected on grounds of that relationship.
4
Contrast with the general rule
Normally, if a grandfather testifies for his grandson against another person (not the son), it would be rejected because the relationship exists. But here, the testimony is against the son, which challenges the son's denial.
The ruling is specific to this situation where the grandson's lineage is in question.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والولد) لأبويه وجديه وعكسه) أي لم تقبل شهادة الفرع لأصله والأصل لفرعه للحديث، ولأن المنافع بين الأولاد والآباء متصلة ولهذا لا يجوز أداء الزكاة إليهم فتكون شهادة لنفسه من وجه وأطلق الولد فشمل الولد من وجه فلا تقبل شهادة ولد الملاعن لأصوله أو هو له أو لفرعه لثبوته من وجه بدليل صحة دعوته منه وعدمها من غيره، وتحرم مناكحته ووضع الزكاة فيه فأحكام البنوة ثابتة له إلا الإرث والنفقة من الطرفين كولد العاهر. ولو باع أحد التوأمين وقد ولدا في ملكه وأعتقه المشتري فشهد البائعة تقبل؛ فإن ادعى الباقي ثبت نسبهما وانتقض البيع والعتق والقضاء ويرد ما قبض أو مثله إن هلك للاستناد لتحويل العقد، وإن كان القضاء قصاصاً في طرف أو نفس فأرشه عليه دون العاقلة وتمامه في تلخيص الجامع من باب شهادة ولد الملاعنة ولا تقبل شهادة ولد أم الولد المنفي من السيد ولا يعطيه الزكاة كولد الحرة المنفي باللعان؛ كذا في المحيط البرهاني. وفي فتح القدير : تجوز شهادته لابنه رضاعاً. وفي خزانة الأكمل : شهد ابناه أن الطالب أبرأ أباهما واحتال بدينه على فلان لم تجز إذا كان الطالب منكراً، وإن كان المال على غير أبيهما فشهدوا أن الطالب أحال به أباهما والطالب ينكر والمطلوب يدعي البراءة والحوالة جازت ا هـ. وفي المحيط البرهاني : إذا شهدا على فعل أبيهما فعلاً ملزماً لا تقبل إذا كان للأب فيه منفعة اتفاقاً وإلا فعلى قولهما لا تقبل وعن محمد روايتان. فلو قال إن كلمك فلان فأنت حر فادعى فلان أنه كلمه وشهد ابناه به لم تقبل عندهما، وكذا إذا علق عتقه بدخوله الدار، ولو أنكر الأب جازت شهادتهما. وكذا الحكم في كل شيء كان من فعل الأب من نكاح أو طلاق أو بيع، وإن شهد ابنا الوكيل على عقد الوكيل فهو على ثلاثة أوجه الأوّل أن يقر الموكل والوكيل بالأمر والعقد وهو على وجهين : فإن ادعاه الخصم قضى القاضي بالتصادق لا بالشهادة، وإن أنكر فعلى قولهما لا تقبل ولا يقضى بشيء إلا في الخلع فإنه يقضى بالطلاق بغير مال لإقرار الزوج به وهو الموكل. وعن محمد يقضى بالعقد إلا بعقد ترجع حقوقه إلى العاقد كالبيع. الثاني أن ينكر الوكيل والموكل فإن جحد الخصم لا تقبل وإلا تقبل اتفاقاً. الثالث أن يقر الوكيل بهما ويجحد الموكل العقد فقط فإن ادعاه الخصم يقضى بالعقود كلها إلا النكاح على قول أبي حنيفة وتمامه فيه . وقيد بالشهادة لهم لأن الشهادة على أصله وفرعه مقبولة إلا إذا شهد الجد على ابنه لابن ابنه قلنا إنها لا تقبل لوجود المانع من المشهود له. وفي المحيط قال محمد: رجل شهد لابن ابنه على أبيه تقبل لأنه حين شهد عليه لم يصر جداً لولده بل يصير جداً بعد حكم الحاكم بشهادته فحينئذ جداً يصير بموجب الشهادة والشيء لا ينفي موجب نفسه ا هـ . وهذا التعليل يفيد أن الكلام في شهادة الأب على إقرار ابنه بأن ما ولدته زوجته ابنه لا
His saying: (and the child) for his parents and grandparents and vice versa means the testimony of a descendant for his ascendant and the ascendant for his descendant is not accepted, due to the hadith, and because the benefits between children and parents are connected, and therefore paying zakat to them is not permissible, so it would be testimony for himself in a sense. And he used the general term 'child' which includes the child [established] in one respect, so the testimony of a child of a mula'an (husband who invoked li'an) for his ascendants or for him or for his descendant is not accepted, because he is [a child] in one respect, as evidenced by the validity of his claiming lineage from him and its invalidity from others, and marriage with him is prohibited, and placing zakat on him [is forbidden]. So the rulings of filiation are established for him except inheritance and maintenance from both sides, like the child of a fornicator. And if one of the twins is sold while they were born in his ownership, and the buyer emancipates him, then the seller testifies, it is accepted; but if the remaining one claims [lineage], both their lineages are established, and the sale and emancipation and judgment are rescinded, and he returns what he took or its like if it perished, due to the contract being overturned. And if the judgment was qisas on a limb or life, then the compensation is upon him, not on the 'aqila. The complete discussion is in Talkhis al-Jami' from the chapter on testimony of the child of a mula'anah. And the testimony of a child of an umm walad who is denied by the master is not accepted, nor is zakat given to him, like the child of a free woman denied by li'an; as in al-Muhit al-Burhani. In Fath al-Qadir: his testimony for his son by rada' is permissible. In Khizanat al-Akmal: His two sons testified that the claimant released their father from debt and transferred his debt to so-and-so, it is not allowed if the claimant denies; but if the debt was on someone other than their father and they testified that the claimant transferred it to their father, while the claimant denies and the defendant claims innocence and the transfer, it is allowed. In al-Muhit al-Burhani: If they testify concerning an act of their father that is binding, it is not accepted if the father has benefit in it by agreement; otherwise, according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] it is not accepted, and from Muhammad there are two narrations. So if he says, 'If so-and-so speaks to you, you are free,' then so-and-so claims he spoke to him, and his two sons testify to it, it is not accepted according to the two. Similarly, if he suspends his emancipation on his entering the house. And if the father denies, their testimony is accepted. The same ruling applies to everything that is an act of the father, such as marriage, divorce, or sale. And if the two sons of the agent testify concerning the agent's contract, it has three aspects. First, that the principal and the agent both affirm the matter and the contract; this has two aspects: if the opponent claims, the judge decides based on mutual confirmation, not testimony; if he denies, according to the two it is not accepted, and nothing is decided, except in khul' where divorce is decided without compensation due to the husband's admission. And from Muhammad: the contract is decided, except for a contract whose rights revert to the contracting party, like sale. Second, that the agent and the principal both deny; if the opponent denies, it is not accepted; otherwise, it is accepted by agreement. Third, that the agent affirms both and the principal denies only the contract; if the opponent claims, all contracts are decided except for marriage according to Abu Hanifa. And he restricted it to testimony for them because testimony against one's ascendant and descendant is accepted, except when the grandfather testifies against his son for his grandson: we say it is not accepted due to the impediment of the beneficiary. In al-Muhit, Muhammad said: A man testified for his grandson against his father; it is accepted, because when he testified against him, he was not a grandfather for his son; he becomes a grandfather only after the judge's ruling based on his testimony; then at that point he becomes a grandfather by virtue of the testimony, and a thing does not negate its own necessary consequence. This reasoning indicates that the discussion is about the testimony of a father concerning his son's admission that what his wife gave birth to is his son.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn's ruling that the testimony of a child for his parents and grandparents, and vice versa, is not accepted. The reason given is a hadith and the fact that mutual benefits are intertwined, making testimony akin to testifying for oneself. The definition of 'child' (walad) includes a child of li'an (mula'an) because he is considered a child in one respect (lineage is established only from the father, not from the accuser). Thus, his testimony for or against his ascendants is not accepted, except that inheritance and maintenance are not established between them. The text then explores various scenarios and exceptions. For example, the testimony of a father for his son against a claim of twin lineage is examined in a complex case involving sale and emancipation. It is accepted only if the remaining twin does not claim lineage. The testimony of a child of an umm walad (slave mother) who is denied by the master is not accepted, like the child of a free woman denied by li'an. However, there is an exception: testimony for a son by rada' (fosterage) is permitted. The passage then discusses at length the testimony of children regarding their father's actions or contracts, with differences between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. For instance, if a father makes a conditional emancipation dependent on someone speaking to him, and his sons testify that the condition occurred, their testimony is not accepted if the father might benefit. But if the father denies the condition, their testimony is accepted. The discussion extends to the testimony of the sons of an agent concerning the principal's contract, with three detailed scenarios. Finally, a special case is given: a grandfather testifying for his grandson (son's son) against his own son. According to Muhammad, this is accepted because at the time of testimony he is not yet a grandfather; he becomes a grandfather only after the testimony is accepted. Therefore, the impediment (being a grandfather as the beneficiary) does not exist when the testimony is given.

Key Terms
الجد (al-jadd): Grandfather (father's father).
ابن الابن (ibn al-ibn): Son's son (grandson).

B) Because the grandfather becomes an ascendant only after the testimony is accepted.
C) Because the testimony is against the son, not for the grandson.
D) Because the grandfather is rich and has no benefit.

Key Takeaway
A grandfather can testify for his grandson against his son because the ascendant relationship is created by the testimony itself.

Shahadat — Testimony
