Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
The Principle of Rejecting Self-Interested Testimony
States a principle and lists numerous applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that testimony bringing benefit or repelling loss is rejected due to suspicion, and apply it to identify which witnesses are disqualified in partnership, employment, and agency cases.

Core Idea
Any testimony that directly benefits the witness or prevents harm is inadmissible due to suspicion of bias.

This lesson unpacks a cornerstone of Hanafi testimony law: self-interest taints testimony. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq states the rule and applies it to partnerships, employees, agents, and more. By understanding the rationale (tuhma), you will predict which testimonies are accepted and which are rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Locate the sentence: 'kull shahada jarra maghnaman aw dafa'a maghraman lam tuqbal lil-tuhma.' Understand key terms: maghnam (benefit), maghram (loss), tuhma (suspicion).
2
Analyze the partnership application
The passage begins with partnership testimony. Recognize that partners in 'inan and mufawadah are treated differently. Partnership matters create suspicion because the witness has a stake in the outcome.
3
Examine the three ways partners can testify about a joint debt
The text gives three scenarios: specifying partnership (rejected), severing partnership (accepted), and general statement (rejected). The logic: when testimony shows no joint interest, suspicion is removed.
4
Apply the principle to employees
Distinguish between ajir khas (special employee) whose testimony is rejected, and ajir mushtarak (general employee) whose testimony is accepted. The reason: ajir khas earns by time, so testifying during work hours creates suspicion.
5
Explore other applications and exceptions
The passage lists many cases: hirer, borrower, depositary, agent, seller's son, etc. For each, identify whether the testimony brings benefit or repels harm, and thus whether it is accepted or rejected.
Pay attention to the distinctions: e.g., agent for marriage (accepted) vs. depositary (rejected).
6
Resolve subsidiary issues and waqf testimony
The text discusses bequests to tribes, households, and neighbors, and whether witnesses who are beneficiaries can testify. Recognize that if the witness has a direct vested interest, testimony is rejected; if indirect or severable, it may be accepted.
Also note the dispute about madrasah waqf testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل لا يدخل في الشركة إلا الدراهم والدنانير ولا يدخل فيه العقار ولا العروض ولهذا قالوا : لو وهب لأحدهما مال غير الدراهم والدنانير لا تبطل الشركة لأن المساواة فيه ليست بشرط وما ذكره في النهاية هو صريح كلام محمد في الأصل كما ذكره في المحيط البرهاني ثم قال : وشهادة أحد شريكي العنان فيما لم يكن من تجارتهما مقبولة لا فيما كان منها، ولم يذكر هذا التفصيل في المفاوضة لأن العنان قد يكون خاصاً وقد يكون عاماً، وأما المفاوضة فلا تكون إلا في جميع الأموال وقد عرف ذلك في كتاب الشركة وعلى قياس ما ذكره شيخ الإسلام في كتاب الشركة أن المفاوضة تكون خاصة يجب أن تكون المفاوضة على التفصيل الذي ذكرنا في العنان ا هـ . وشمل كلام المؤلف ما إذا شهدا أن لهما ولفلان على هذا الرجل ألف درهم فهي على ثلاثة أوجه الأول أن ينصا على الشركة فلا تقبل. الثاني أن ينصا على قطع الشركة بأن قالا نشهد أن لفلان على هذا خمسمائة بسبب على حدة ولنا عليه ضمانه بسبب على حدة فتقبل الثالث أن يطلقا فلا تقبل لاحتمال الاشتراك. ولو كان لواحد على ثلاثة دين فشهد اثنان أن الدائن أبرأهما وفلاناً عن الألف، فإن كانوا كفلاء لم تقبل وإلا فإن شهدوا بالإبراء بكلمة واحدة فكذلك وإلا تقبل ؛ كذا في المحيط البرهاني. وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله إلى قاعدة في الشهادات وهي أن كل شهادة جرت مغنماً أو دفعت مغرماً لم تقبل للتهمة فلا تقبل شهادة المستأجر للأجير بالمستأجر والمستعير للمعير بالمستعار، وشهادة الأجير الخاص كأجير المياومة والمشاهرة لا العام كالخياط لمن استأجره فتقبل. ولا تقبل شهادة ذابح الشاة المأمور بذبحها لمدعيها على غاصبها ولا شهادة ابن البائع على أن الشفيع طلب الشفعة من المشتري، ولا شهادة المودع بها، وتقبل شهادة الوكيل بالنكاح بالطلاق، والوكيل بالشراء بالعتق، وشهادة ابن البائع على الشفيع بتسليم الشفعة إلى المشتري ولا تقبل على أن المشتري سلمها إلى الشفيع، ولا تقبل شهادة البائع على أن المشتري أعتق العبد، ولا شهادة المعتق بقدر الثمن إذا اختلفا، وتقبل إذا شهد بإيفاء الثمن أو إبراء البائع ولا تقبل شهادة المودع والمستعير والمستأجر للمدعي قبل الرد وتقبل شهادة المرتهن ولو شهد المودع أو المستأجر للعبد بإعتاق مولاه أو تدبيره أو كتابته عند دعواه جازت لا ببيعه وتمام تفريعاته في المحيط . وهنا مسائل متفرعة على عدم شهادة الشريك لشريكه : الأولى شهدا أن زيداً أوصى بثلث ماله بني فلان وهما من تلك القبيلة صحت ولا شيء لهما منها . الثانية لو أوصى لفقراء قبيلته وهما منهم فالحكم كذلك الثالث لو أوصى لفقراء بيته أو لأهل بيته وهما منهم لم يصح ولو كانا غنيين ،صحت والفرق بين الأوليين والثالثة أنه يجوز فيهما تخصيص البعض في الثالثة . الرابعة لو أوصى لفقراء جيرانه فشهد من له أولاد محتاجون منهم لم في حق الأولاد وغيرهم، والفرق بينهما وبين أولادهما أن المخاطب لم يدخل عموم خطابه فلم يتناولهما الكلام بخلاف الأولاد فإنهم داخلون تحت الشهادة، وإنما أدخلنا المتكلم في مسألة الشهادة لفقراء أهل بيته باعتبار أنهم يحصون بخلاف فقراء جيرانه وبني تميم، وذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه من الوقف لو شهدا أنها صدقة موقوفة على فقراء جيرانه وهما منهم جازت، ولو على فقراء قرابته لا . قال الناطفي في الفرق : إن القرابة لا تزول والجوار يزول فلم يكن شهادة لنفسه لا محالة ا هـ . وأهل بيت الإنسان لا يزول عنهم الاسم لأنهم أقاربه الذين في عياله فلهذا لم تقبل فيها، ولكن يشكل بمسألة القبيلة فإن الاسم عنهم لا يزول مع قبولها ولكن لا يدخلون، ويمكن الفرق بين الوصية والوقف بما أشار إليه ابن الشحنة . وقال قاضيخان عقب ما نقلته عنه : فعلى هذا شهادة أهل المدرسة بوقفها جائزة. وقال في موضع آخر : وأما أصحاب المدرسة إذا شهدوا بالوقف على المدرسة قال بعضهم إن كان الشاهد يطلب لنفسه حقاً من ذلك لا تقبل وإلا تقبل قياساً على مسألة الشفعة لو شهد بعض الشفعاء بالبيع فإن كان لا يطلبها تقبل قال رضي الله تعالى عنه : وعندي هذا يخالف الشفعة لأن حق الشفعة مما يحتمل الإبطال أما الوقف على المدرسة من كان فقيراً من أصحاب المدرسة يكون مستحقاً للوقف استحقاقاً لا يبطل بإبطاله فإنه إذا قال أبطلت حقي كان له أن يطلب ويأخذ بعد ذلك فكان شاهداً لنفسه فيجب أن لا تقبل ا هـ . وتعقبه الطرسو فيه نظر لأن الفقيه من أهل المدرسة يمكنه أن يعزل نفسه فلا تبقى له وظيفة أصلاً فكيف يقول لا يمكنه إبطاله؟ ورده ابن وهبان بأن هذا الاعتراض ليس بشيء فإن الواقف إذا وقف على من اتصف بصفة الفقه والفقر مثلاً والإقامة استحق من اجتمعت فيه شرائط الوقف، ولا لأستاذه رسوسي بقوله مردودة وهي رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله. قالوا: إن كان الأجير مشتركاً تجوز شهادته في الروايات كلها، وما ذكر في الديات محمول على هذا الوجه وإن كان أجير وحد مشاهرة أو مسانهة أو مياومة لا تقبل شهادته لأستاذه لا في تجارته ولا في شيء آخر، وما ذكر في الكفالة محمول على هذا؛ كذا ذكر الناطفي والصدر الإمام الأجل الشهيد ووجهه ظاهر لأن أجير الوحد يستحق الأجر بمضي الزمان وإذا كان يستوجب الأجر لزمان أداء الشهادة كان متهماً فيما شهد، أما الأجير المشترك لا يستوجب الأجر إلا بالعمل الذي عقدت عليه الإجارة فإذا لم يستوجب بشهادته أجراً انتفت التهمة عن شهادته ولهذا جازت شهادة القابلة على الولادة عند شرطها وهو العدالة اهـ .
The Book of Testimonies, Chapter on Whose Testimony is Accepted and Whose is Not. Only dirhams and dinars enter into partnership; real estate and goods do not enter. Hence they said: If one of them is gifted property other than dirhams and dinars, the partnership is not annulled because equality in it is not a condition. What was mentioned in al-Nihayah is the explicit statement of Muhammad in al-Asl, as mentioned in al-Muhit al-Burhani. Then he said: The testimony of one of the partners in an 'inan partnership in what is not from their trade is accepted, not in what is from it. He did not mention this detail for mufawadah because 'inan may be specific or general, whereas mufawadah is only in all wealth, as known in the book of partnership. By analogy with what Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in the book of partnership, that mufawadah is specific, it must be that mufawadah follows the detail we mentioned for 'inan. The author's words include if they testify that they and so-and-so have one thousand dirhams against this man: this is in three ways. First, they specify partnership: not accepted. Second, they specify severance of partnership by saying, 'We testify that so-and-so has five hundred against him separately, and we have his guarantee against him separately': it is accepted. Third, they leave it general: not accepted due to possibility of partnership. If one person has a debt against three, and two testify that the creditor has discharged them and so-and-so from the thousand, if they were guarantors it is not accepted. Otherwise, if they testify to the discharge in one word, similarly; otherwise it is accepted. Thus in al-Muhit al-Burhani. The author indicated a principle in testimonies: every testimony that brings benefit or repels harm is not accepted due to suspicion. Thus the testimony of the hirer for the employee against the employer is not accepted, nor of the borrower for the lender against the lender; nor the testimony of the special employee, like the daily or monthly wage earner, as opposed to the general employee, like the tailor for the one who hired him: it is accepted. The testimony of the slaughterer of the sheep, commanded to slaughter it, for the claimant against the usurper is not accepted; nor the testimony of the seller's son that the preemptor demanded preemption from the buyer; nor the testimony of the depositary concerning the deposit. The testimony of the agent for marriage regarding divorce is accepted, and of the agent for purchase regarding manumission, and of the seller's son that the preemptor surrendered preemption to the buyer, but not that the buyer surrendered it to the preemptor. The testimony of the seller that the buyer manumitted the slave is not accepted, nor the testimony of the manumitter about the price if they differ. It is accepted if he testifies to payment of the price or the seller's discharge. The testimony of the depositary, borrower, and hirer for the claimant before return is not accepted; the testimony of the pledgee is accepted. If the depositary or hirer testifies for the slave regarding his master's manumission, tadbir, or kitabah when he claims it, it is permitted, not regarding his sale. All its branches are in al-Muhit. Here are subsidiary issues branching from the non-acceptance of a partner's testimony for his partner. First: If they testify that Zayd bequeathed one-third of his wealth to Banu so-and-so, and they are from that tribe, it is valid and they have nothing from it. Second: If he bequeathed to the poor of his tribe and they are among them, the ruling is likewise. Third: If he bequeathed to the poor of his household or his family and they are among them, it is not valid, but if they were rich, it is valid. The difference between the first two and the third is that specification of some is allowed in the first two, but not in the third. Fourth: If he bequeathed to the poor of his neighbors, and one who has needy children among them testifies, it is not valid regarding the children and others. The difference between them and their children is that the addressee did not include the general address, so the speech did not include them, unlike the children who are included under the testimony. We included the speaker in the issue of testimony for the poor of his household because they are countable, unlike the poor of his neighbors or Banu Tamim. Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatawa: regarding a waqf, if they testify that it is a sadaqah waqf for the poor of his neighbors and they are among them, it is valid; but if for the poor of his relatives, not. Al-Natifi said in the distinction: Kinship does not cease, while neighborliness ceases, so it is not testimony for oneself inevitably. The people of a man's household do not lose their name because they are his relatives in his care; thus it is not accepted. But this is problematic with the issue of the tribe, for their name does not cease yet it is accepted, but they are not included. A distinction can be made between bequest and waqf by what Ibn al-Shihnah indicated. Qadikhan said after what I quoted: On this basis, the testimony of the people of a madrasah regarding its waqf is permissible. He said elsewhere: As for the people of the madrasah, if they testify about the waqf on the madrasah, some said: If the witness seeks a right for himself from it, it is not accepted; otherwise it is accepted, by analogy with the issue of preemption, if one of the preemptors testifies to the sale, if he does not seek preemption it is accepted. Radi Allah Ta'ala said: In my view, this contradicts preemption because the right of preemption can be annulled, whereas the waqf on the madrasah—anyone who is poor among the people of the madrasah becomes entitled to the waqf with an entitlement that cannot be annulled by his annulment, for if he says 'I annul my right,' he can still request and take thereafter, so he is testifying for himself and thus must not be accepted. Al-Tarsusi criticized him: There is consideration, because the faqih among the people of the madrasah can resign his position so he has no function at all, so how can he say he cannot annul it? Ibn Wahban refuted him: This objection is nothing, because if the waqif makes a waqf on those who possess the description of jurisprudence, poverty, and residence, then whoever fulfills the conditions of the waqf becomes entitled, and his right does not cease by his mere declaration. ... And the narration from al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa is rejected. They said: If the employee is a general employee (ajir mushtarak), his testimony is permissible in all narrations. What was mentioned in diyat is interpreted in this sense. If he is a single employee (ajir wahid) for a month, year, or day, his testimony is not accepted for his master, neither in his trade nor in anything else. What was mentioned in kafalah is interpreted in this sense. Thus mentioned al-Natifi and al-Sadr al-Imam al-Ajal al-Shahid. Its reason is clear: the single employee earns wages by the passage of time, and if he earns wages for the time of giving testimony, he is suspect regarding what he testified. As for the general employee, he earns wages only by the work for which the hire was contracted; if he does not earn wages for his testimony, suspicion is removed, and hence the testimony of the midwife regarding childbirth is permissible when she has the condition of uprightness.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed exposition of a fundamental principle in Hanafi testimony law: any testimony that directly brings a material benefit to the witness or repels a material harm from him is rejected due to suspicion (tuhma) of self-interest. The passage begins by discussing partnership testimony, clarifying that only dirhams and dinars enter into partnership, so gifts of other property do not invalidate the partnership. The testimony of a partner in an 'inan partnership is accepted regarding matters outside the partnership business, but not regarding matters within it. This detail applies analogously to mufawadah partnership. The author then enunciates the general principle and provides numerous specific applications: the hirer cannot testify for the employee against the employer, the borrower for the lender, the special employee (e.g., daily or monthly wage earner) for the one who hired him, but a general employee (e.g., a tailor) can. Further examples involve the slaughterer of a sheep, the seller's son in preemption cases, the depositary, and the agent for marriage or purchase. The passage also delves into subsidiary issues related to partner testimony, including bequests to tribes, households, and neighbors, and the distinction between bequest and waqf. A significant discussion concerns the testimony of residents of a madrasah about its waqf, with differing views on whether their personal interest disqualifies them. The passage concludes with an analysis of employee testimony, distinguishing between the special employee (ajir wahid) who earns wages by time and is thus suspect, and the general employee (ajir mushtarak) who earns only by work done and is not suspect. The midwife's testimony on childbirth is given as an example. Throughout, the commentary explains the rationale of avoiding suspicion of bias, which is the bedrock of these rulings.

Key Terms
شركة العنان (shirkat al-'inan): A partnership where each partner contributes capital but is only an agent in the specific trade they agreed upon, not in all wealth.
شركة المفاوضة (shirkat al-mufawadah): A partnership of full agency and guarantee where partners are equal in all wealth and authority.
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A special employee who is hired for a fixed period (daily, monthly, yearly) and earns wages by the passage of time.
قاعدة (qa'idah): A legal maxim or principle that governs multiple rulings; here, the principle that self-interested testimony is rejected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A special employee (ajir khas) witnesses a contract between his employer and a third party. According to the Hanafi principle, his testimony is:
A) Accepted because he is an upright Muslim.
B) Not accepted because he earns wages by time, creating suspicion.
C) Accepted only if he testifies outside working hours.
D) Not accepted because employees lack legal capacity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that testimony bringing benefit or repelling loss is rejected due to suspicion of self-interest governs a wide range of cases, from partners to employees to beneficiaries of waqf.

Testimony of Hired Workers: The Distinction Between Ajir Wahd and Ajir Mushtarak
Ruling on acceptance of testimony from a hired worker testifying for his employer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ajir wahd and ajir mushtarak and state the ruling on the acceptance of their testimony in the Hanafi school, applying the principle of tuhma (suspicion of partiality).

Core Idea
A time-based hired worker's testimony is rejected due to self-interest; a task-based worker's testimony is accepted because no such interest exists.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a nuanced Hanafi ruling regarding the testimony of hired workers. The key is not the mere fact of employment but the nature of the wage contract. Understanding the 'illa (effective cause) – whether the witness stands to gain financially from testifying – allows you to apply this ruling consistently across various scenarios, as demonstrated by the example of the midwife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Note the two types: ajir wahd (time-based, e.g., monthly/daily hire) and ajir mushtarak (task-based, e.g., midwife, tailor).
The Arabic terms are key: 'أجير وحد' and 'أجير مشترك'.
2
State the ruling for each
For ajir wahd: testimony is rejected (لا تقبل). For ajir mushtarak: testimony is accepted (تجوز) in all narrations.
The text explicitly says 'في الروايات كلها' for ajir mushtarak, indicating consensus.
3
Locate the reasoning (wajh)
The 'illa is tuhma: ajir wahd earns wages during the time of testimony, creating a conflict of interest; ajir mushtarak does not earn by testifying.
This is a clear qiyas jaliyyah based on the presence/absence of financial gain.
4
Relate the example of the midwife
The midwife (qabila) is an ajir mushtarak; her testimony about birth is accepted if she is upright (adala), as she does not earn wages by testifying.
This illustrates the practical application of the rule.
5
Compare with other madhhabs
Shafi'is may accept testimony of any hired worker if he is upright, without this distinction. Hanafis insist on the tuhma analysis.
The cross-madhhab difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله. قالوا: إن كان الأجير مشتركاً تجوز شهادته في الروايات كلها، وما ذكر في الديات محمول على هذا الوجه وإن كان أجير وحد مشاهرة أو مسانهة أو مياومة لا تقبل شهادته لأستاذه لا في تجارته ولا في شيء آخر، وما ذكر في الكفالة محمول على هذا؛ كذا ذكر الناطفي والصدر الإمام الأجل الشهيد ووجهه ظاهر لأن أجير الوحد يستحق الأجر بمضي الزمان وإذا كان يستوجب الأجر لزمان أداء الشهادة كان متهماً فيما شهد، أما الأجير المشترك لا يستوجب الأجر إلا بالعمل الذي عقدت عليه الإجارة فإذا لم يستوجب بشهادته أجراً انتفت التهمة عن شهادته ولهذا جازت شهادة القابلة على الولادة عند شرطها وهو العدالة اهـ .
The narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. They said: If the hired worker is a common [task-based] worker (ajir mushtarak), his testimony is permissible in all narrations. What is mentioned in the chapter of blood money (diyat) is carried upon this [interpretation]. But if he is a hired worker for a fixed period (ajir wahd), monthly, yearly, or daily, his testimony for his employer is not accepted, whether in his trade or in anything else. What is mentioned in the chapter of surety (kafala) is carried upon this. Thus mentioned al-Natafi and al-Sadr al-Imam al-Ajall al-Shahid. Its reasoning is apparent: because the fixed-period worker (ajir wahd) earns his wage by the passage of time, and if he earns wages for the time he gives testimony, he is under suspicion (tuhma) regarding what he testifies. As for the common worker (ajir mushtarak), he earns his wage only by the work for which the contract of hire was made; if he does not earn wages by his testimony, suspicion is removed from his testimony. For this reason, the testimony of the midwife (qabila) regarding birth is allowed when her condition is [fulfilled], namely uprightness (adala).
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad's transmission from Abu Hanifa regarding the testimony of hired workers. It distinguishes two types of hired workers: 

1. Ajir Wahd (exclusive hired worker): hired for a fixed period (time-based), e.g., monthly, yearly, or daily. His wage is earned simply by the passage of time, regardless of actual work. If he testifies for his employer during his hire period, he is suspected of testifying to please his employer to continue his wage, thus his testimony is rejected (la tuqbal).

2. Ajir Mushtarak (common hired worker): hired to perform a specific task (e.g., a midwife delivering a child, a tailor sewing a shirt). His wage is earned only by performing the contracted work; giving testimony does not earn him additional wage. Therefore, no suspicion attaches, and his testimony is accepted (tajuz).

The passage notes that this ruling is consistent in all narrations (fi al-riwayat kulliha). It also clarifies that similar rulings in chapters on diyat (blood money) and kafala (surety) are to be interpreted based on this distinction. The reasoning (wajh) is explained: the ajir wahd's self-interest is evident because his wage depends on the time period, including the time he gives testimony; the ajir mushtarak has no such interest.

The example given is the midwife (qabila): she is a common worker hired to assist in childbirth; her testimony about the birth is accepted provided she is upright (adala), as she does not earn wages by testifying.

Key Terms
أجير وحد (ajīr waḥd): A hired worker whose work is defined by a fixed period (time-based hire); his wage is earned by the passage of time regardless of actual work.
أجير مشترك (ajīr mushtarak): A hired worker contracted to perform a specific task; his wage is earned only upon completion of the task.
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion of partiality or self-interest that disqualifies a witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is the testimony of a task-based hired worker (ajir mushtarak) accepted while that of a time-based (ajir wahd) is not?
A) Because ajir mushtarak is more trustworthy.
B) Because ajir wahd earns wages during the time he testifies, creating a conflict of interest.
C) Because the employer prefers ajir mushtarak.
D) Because the text does not provide a reason.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a hired worker's testimony hinges on whether he earns wages during the act of testifying, not merely on his employment status.

Testimony of Waqf Beneficiaries: The Hanafi Ruling of Acceptance (Mu'tamad)
Detailed exposition of rulings on testimony by waqf beneficiaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of waqf beneficiaries and explain the distinction between permanent and temporary relationships that affects acceptance.

Core Idea
A waqf beneficiary's testimony is accepted if the relationship is temporary or the right can be renounced, removing the accusation of self-interest.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a nuanced area: when can a person who stands to benefit from a waqf serve as a witness to establish that very waqf? The Hanafi school, through a series of fatwas and distinctions, arrived at a relied-upon position that such testimony is generally accepted, contrary to an initial presumption. The key lies in understanding the nature of the witness's connection to the waqf—whether it is permanent (like kinship) or temporary (like neighborhood or studentship)—and whether the entitlement can be effectively renounced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The core question: Is the testimony of a person who is a beneficiary of a waqf valid when testifying about that waqf? The default concern is tuhma (accusation of self-interest).
2
Recognize the underlying legal cause (illa)
The illa for rejection is the witness's self-interest (tuhma). If the witness stands to gain directly from the outcome, the testimony is suspect. The Hanafis analyze whether this tuhma can be eliminated.
Tuhma is a key concept in Hanafi shahada law.
3
Distinguish permanent vs. temporary relationships
Permanent relationships (like kinship) create perpetual tuhma because the benefit is intrinsic. Temporary relationships (like neighborhood or studentship) can end, so the tuhma is not inevitable. This distinction is made by al-Natafi and others.
Qadi Khan's fatwa: testimony accepted for neighborhood waqf, rejected for kinship waqf.
4
Examine the analogy to pre-emption (shuf'a)
Qadi Khan analogizes the waqf beneficiary to a pre-emptor: if the pre-emptor testifies but does not claim his right, it is accepted. Similarly, if the waqf beneficiary does not actively seek a personal right at the time of testimony, it is accepted.
This analogy is contested by later scholars who argue that waqf entitlement is more permanent.
5
Resolve the intra-madhhab conflict: the mufta bihi
After extensive debate, the relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) is that such testimony is accepted (al-qabul fi al-kull), provided the witness is not actively seeking a personal right from that testimony at the moment. This is affirmed by al-Bazzaziyyah and the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
The qualification about seeking a right comes from Qadi Khan's second ruling and is incorporated into the final position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل جيرانه وهما منهم فالحكم كذلك الثالث لو أوصى لفقراء بيته أو لأهل بيته وهما منهم لم يصح ولو كانا غنيين صحت والفرق بين الأوليين والثالثة أنه يجوز فيهما تخصيص البعض في الثالثة . الرابعة لو أوصى لفقراء جيرانه فشهد من له أولاد محتاجون منهم لم في حق الأولاد وغيرهم، والفرق بينهما وبين أولادهما أن المخاطب لم يدخل عموم خطابه فلم يتناولهما الكلام بخلاف الأولاد فإنهم داخلون تحت الشهادة، وإنما أدخلنا المتكلم في مسألة الشهادة لفقراء أهل بيته باعتبار أنهم يحصون بخلاف فقراء جيرانه وبني تميم، وذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه من الوقف لو شهدا أنها صدقة موقوفة على فقراء جيرانه وهما منهم بوقفها جائزة. وقال في موضع آخر : وأما أصحاب المدرسة إذا شهدوا بالوقف على المدرسة قال بعضهم إن كان الشاهد يطلب لنفسه حقاً . من ذلك لا تقبل وإلا تقبل قياساً على مسألة الشفعة لو شهد بعض الشفعاء بالبيع فإن كان لا يطلبها تقبل قال رضي الله تعالى عنه : وعندي هذا يخالف الشفعة لأن حق الشفعة مما يحتمل الإبطال أما الوقف على المدرسة من كان فقيراً من أصحاب المدرسة يكون مستحقاً للوقف استحقاقاً لا يبطل بإبطاله فإنه إذا قال أبطلت حقي كان له أن يطلب ويأخذ بعد ذلك فكان شاهداً لنفسه فيجب أن لا تقبل ا هـ . وتعقبه الطرسو فيه نظر لأن الفقيه من أهل المدرسة يمكنه أن يعزل نفسه فلا تبقى له وظيفة أصلاً فكيف يقول لا يمكنه إبطاله؟ ورده ابن وهبان بأن هذا الاعتراض ليس بشيء فإن الواقف إذا وقف على من اتصف بصفة الفقه والفقر مثلاً والإقامة استحق من اجتمعت فيه شرائط الوقف، ولا لاستاذه رسوسي بقوله مردودة . اعتبار بعزله نفسه بل لو عزل نفسه في كل يوم مائة مرة ثم طلب أخذ كالوقف على الابن إذا عزل نفسه عن الوقف فإنه لا ينعزل، وصاحب الفوائد لم يفهم هذا من كلام قاضيخان بل جرى على عادة أوقاف المدارس في بلادنا فإن الواقف يجعل النظر فيه إلى الحاكم مثلاً أو إلى الناظر ويجعل له ولاية العزل والتقرير والإعطاء والحرمان من اتصف بصفة الفقة على مذهب من المذاهب، فحينئذ إذا أبطل ذلك حقه وعزل نفسه صح وليس له العود إلا أن يقرره الحاكم أو من له ولاية التقرير وليس كلام قاضيخان في ذلك بل كلامه فيمن وقف الواقف عليه وذلك يستحق ما وقف عليه الواقف ولا يبطل بإبطاله له ا هـ . وفيما قال نظر لي لأن الواقف إذا وقف على الفقهاء مثلاً فإن الفقيه لا يستحق في ذلك الريع إلا بالتقرير ممن له ولايته، وكذا على الفقراء لا أنه يستحق من كان فقيهاً أو فقيراً مطلقاً كما توهمه ابن وهبان لأن الفقيه والفقير الطالب لم يتعينا ولا يمكن أن ينصرف إلى كل فقيه وكل فقير وإنما هو للجنس ويتعين بالتقرير فالحق أن من أسقط حقه من وظيفة تقرر فيها فإنه يسقط حقه، سواء كان الوقف على جنس الفقهاء أو على عدد معين منهم كما هو في أوقاف القاهرة. وإن أسقط حقه من وقف على الفقهاء والفقراء بلا تعيين ولم يقرر في وقفهم لم يصح لعدم تعينه فللناظر أن يقرره بعده ويعطيه ما خصه لأنه يطلب ويأخذ بتقرير، فمعنى الاستحقاق الذي لا يبطل بالإبطال في كلام قاضيخان جواز أن يقرر بعد إبطاله ويعطى بعده من وقف على الفقهاء، ومعنى قول الطرسوسي أنه يبطل بعزله نفسه إذا كان بعد تقريره وليس هذا كالوقف على الابن كما توهمه ابن وهبان لأن استحقاق الابن لا يتوقف على تقرير بخلاف استحقاق الفقيه كما لا يخفى بقي من جنس المسائل السابقة مسألة لو شهدا على وقف في مكتب فيه أولادهم قيل يصح، وقيل لا والأظهر الصحة لأن كون أولادهم في المكتب غير لازم فلا تكون شهادتهم لهم كشهادة أهل المدرسة وفي وقف الظهيرية بعد أن ذكر مسألة المدرسة وشهادة أهلها وشهادة أهل المحلة في وقف على المحلة ما نصه وكذلك الشهادة على وقف مكتب وللشاهد صبي في المكتب لا تقبل قيل وفي هذ المسائل كلها تقبل وهو الصحيح ا هـ . القبول في البزازية في مسألة المكتب وشهادة أهل المحلة في وقف المسجد صحح وهكذا ا هـ وشهادة الفقهاء على وقفية وقف على مدرسة كذا وهم من أهل تلك المدرسة والشهادة على وقف المسجد الجامع، وكذا أبناء السبيل إذا شهدوا بوقف على أبناء السبيل إلى آخره، فالمعتمد القبول في الكل. وذكر ابن الشحنة بعده تنبيه ومن هذا النمط مسألة قضاء القاضي في وقف تحت نظره أو هو مستحق فيه ا هـ . قلت . تنبيه : الكلام كله في شهادة الفقهاء بأصل الوقف لقولهم شهادة الفقهاء على وقفية قوله : (ومن هذا النمط مسألة قضاء القاضي الخ قال الرملي : يعلم به جواز شهادة الناظر في
Chapter of testimonies: Section on whose testimony is accepted and who is not. [As for] his neighbors, and both of them are among them, the ruling is likewise. Third: If he bequeathed to the poor of his household or to his family members and both of them are among them, it is not valid; but if both were wealthy, it is valid. The difference between the first two [cases] and the third is that it is permissible in them to specify some [beneficiaries], but not in the third. Fourth: If he bequeathed to the poor of his neighbors, and testimony is given by one who has needy children among them, it is not [valid] regarding the children and others. The difference between them and their children is that the addressee [the testator] did not include them in the general address, so the speech does not apply to them, unlike the children who are included under the testimony. We only introduced the speaker in the matter of testimony for the poor of his household because they are [limited and can be counted], unlike the poor of his neighborhood and Banu Tamim. Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa: Regarding waqf, if they testify that it is a charity (sadaqa) endowed upon the poor of his neighborhood and they are among them, it is permissible; but if upon the poor of his relatives, it is not. al-Natafi said in the distinction: Kinship does not cease, while neighborhood ceases, so it is not testimony for himself inevitably. The people of a man's household do not cease to have that name because they are his relatives who are in his household; therefore it is not accepted. But there is a difficulty with the issue of the tribe: the name does not cease for them yet it is accepted? But they are not included. The distinction between bequest and waqf can be made as indicated by Ibn al-Shihnah. Qadi Khan said following what I transmitted from him: On this basis, the testimony of the people of the school (madrasa) regarding its waqf is valid. He said elsewhere: As for the affiliates of the school, if they testify about the endowment on the school, some said: if the witness seeks a right for himself from that, it is not accepted, otherwise it is accepted, by analogy to the issue of pre-emption: if some pre-emptor testifies to the sale, if he does not seek it, it is accepted. Radi Allahu 'anhu said: In my view, this differs from pre-emption because the right of pre-emption can be invalidated, but as for the endowment on the school, whoever is poor among the affiliates of the school has an entitlement that is not invalidated by his invalidating it; for if he says I have invalidated my right, he may demand and take later, so he is testifying for himself and therefore it should not be accepted. Al-Tarasusi objected: There is consideration because the faqih (scholar) among the school affiliates can remove himself (from entitlement) so he has no stipend at all; how can he say he cannot invalidate it? Ibn Wahban replied: This objection is nothing; for the endower, if he endowed upon those characterized by jurisprudence, poverty, and residence, the one in whom the conditions of the waqf are combined becomes entitled. There is no regard to his removing himself, for even if he removes himself a hundred times a day then seeks to take, it is like the endowment on the son: if he removes himself from the endowment, he is not removed. The author of al-Fawa'id did not understand this from Qadi Khan's words but followed the usual practice of endowments of schools in our country, where the endower delegates administration to the judge or supervisor and gives him authority of removal, appointment, giving, and deprivation of those characterized by jurisprudence according to a school of thought. In that case, if he invalidates his right and removes himself, it is valid, and he may not return unless the judge or one with authority reappoints him. Qadi Khan's words are not about that but about one upon whom the endower endowed; he is entitled to what is endowed and it is not invalidated by his invalidating it. There is consideration in what he said because when the endower endows upon jurists, for example, the jurist is not entitled to the revenue except by appointment by one who has authority; similarly for the poor, it is not that he is entitled absolutely as Ibn Wahban imagined, because the jurist and the poor seeker are not specified and it is impossible for it to go to every jurist and every poor person; rather it is for the genus and becomes specified by appointment. The correct view is that one who drops his right from a stipend in which he was appointed, his right drops, whether the endowment is upon the genus of jurists or upon a specific number of them, as is the case in the endowments of Cairo. If he drops his right from an endowment upon jurists and poor without specification and was not appointed in their endowment, it is not valid because of lack of specification; the supervisor may appoint him thereafter and give him what is allocated because he seeks and takes by appointment. So the meaning of entitlement that is not invalidated by invalidation in Qadi Khan's words is the permissibility of being appointed after his invalidation and being given from the endowment upon jurists. And the meaning of al-Tarasusi's statement that it is invalidated by his removal of himself is when it is after his appointment; this is not like the endowment on the son as Ibn Wahban imagined, because the son's entitlement does not depend on appointment, unlike the jurist's entitlement as is not hidden. Remaining from the kind of previous issues: the issue of if they testify upon an endowment in a maktab (kuttab) which includes their children: it was said it is valid, and it was said not, and the most apparent is validity because the presence of their children in the maktab is not permanent, so their testimony is not like the testimony of the school affiliates. In the Waqf al-Zahiriyyah, after mentioning the issue of the school and the testimony of its people and the testimony of the people of the neighborhood (mahalla) regarding the endowment on the neighborhood: likewise, testimony on the endowment of a maktab while the witness has a child in the maktab is not accepted; it was said: in all these issues it is accepted, and that is the correct view. Acceptance is in al-Bazzaziyyah in the issue of the maktab and the testimony of the people of the neighborhood regarding the endowment of the mosque; he corrected it thus. And the testimony of jurists on the waqf of an endowment on such-and-such a school while they are among the people of that school, and testimony on the endowment of the congregational mosque, and similarly wayfarers if they testify upon an endowment on wayfarers, etc. So the relied-upon (mu'tamad) is acceptance in all. Ibn al-Shihnah mentioned after it a note: and from this pattern is the issue of the judge's judgment regarding an endowment under his supervision or in which he is entitled. I said: a note: all the speech is about the testimony of jurists on the original waqf; their statement: testimony of jurists on the waqf. He said: (And from this pattern is the issue of the judge's judgment...) al-Ramli said: one learns from it the permissibility of the testimony of the supervisor (nazir) in
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on rulings regarding acceptance of testimony when the witnesses are themselves beneficiaries of a bequest or endowment. The commentary follows the structure of the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) and expands with fatawa and clarifications.

The first part discusses bequests: if a testator bequeaths to the poor of his household and the witnesses are among them, their testimony is not accepted because they are testifying for themselves (since kinship is permanent) unless they are wealthy (not benefiting). The key distinction is that for bequests to a defined group (like household), the witnesses cannot be benefactors, but for bequests to a general group (like neighbors), the testimony may be accepted because neighborhood is temporary and can cease. Then Qadi Khan's fatawa on waqf are cited: if witnesses testify that a property is an endowment on the poor of their neighborhood and they are among them, their testimony is accepted because neighborhood ceases; but if it is an endowment on their relatives, it is not accepted because kinship is permanent.

The discussion then addresses a conflict: the people of a man's household (his family) also have permanent kinship, so why is testimony accepted for bequests to household but not for waqf? The author indicates a distinction between bequest and waqf as pointed out by Ibn al-Shihnah. Next, Qadi Khan's two statements on testimony of school affiliates are analyzed. The first ruling says testimony of school affiliates regarding the school's waqf is valid. The second ruling distinguishes: if the witness seeks a right for himself (e.g., a stipend), it is rejected; otherwise accepted, by analogy to pre-emption. However, Radi al-Din (the commentator) objects: the analogy fails because in pre-emption the right can be invalidated, but in waqf the entitlement is permanent—the beneficiary cannot truly renounce it, so he is always testifying for himself. Al-Tarasusi then objects: the scholar can actually renounce his entitlement by removing himself, so the objection is invalid. Ibn Wahban responds: the scholar cannot effectively renounce because the entitlement is conditioned on his character; if he tries to renounce, he remains entitled because the condition persists. This triggers a lengthy analysis of the nature of entitlement in such awqaf (endowments on a class vs. specified individuals). The author clarifies that in many actual endowments (like in Cairo), the beneficiary becomes entitled only after appointment (taqrir) by the supervisor, so renunciation is effective. After that, the passage resolves several subsidiary issues: testimony of people of the neighborhood on a neighborhood waqf, testimony on a maktab (school) waqf when the witness's child is a student, testimony of jurists on a school waqf, and testimony of wayfarers. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that all such testimony is accepted (al-qabul fi al-kull). The passage ends with a note by Ibn al-Shihnah extending the principle to a judge testifying about a waqf under his supervision or in which he is a beneficiary, and al-Ramli's confirmation that the supervisor (nazir) may also testify.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Legal testimony before a judge to establish a right
وقف (waqf): Endowment: permanent dedication of property for charitable purposes
مستحق (mustaḥiqq): One who is entitled to benefit from a waqf by meeting the conditions set by the endower
تقرير (taqrīr): Appointment or assignment of a specific stipend to a beneficiary from a waqf
قرابة (qarāba): Kinship relation that is permanent and does not cease

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on the testimony of a school affiliate testifying that the school is a waqf?
A) Always rejected because he is a beneficiary.
B) Rejected only if he seeks a right for himself from that testimony; otherwise accepted.
C) Always accepted because the school is a public good.
D) Rejected unless he is a wealthy person.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mu'tamad accepts testimony of waqf beneficiaries, removing the tuhma through the possibility of renunciation or the temporary nature of the relationship.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony of Connected Persons in Waqf Cases
Rulings on the admissibility of testimony from persons with personal interest in a waqf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on testimony of persons with a connection to a waqf and explain the reasoning based on the absence of direct tuhma.

Core Idea
Testimony of connected persons in waqf cases is accepted unless the connection creates certainty of partiality.

In waqf (endowment) cases, a witness's connection to the beneficiary or the subject matter often raises concerns about bias. However, the Hanafi school draws a nuanced line: mere association does not automatically disqualify a witness. This lesson examines the scenarios where testimony is accepted despite such ties, and the reasoning that settles the ikhtilaf within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Testimony Scenarios
List the four cases mentioned: parents of children in a maktab waqf, fuqaha of a madrasa waqf, residents of a neighborhood waqf, and wayfarers for a wayfarer waqf. Each involves a witness who is part of the beneficiary group.
These are examples of 'connected' witnesses.
2
Understand the Ikhtilaf
Note the two positions: some scholars reject such testimony due to suspicion of partiality (tuhma), while others accept it. The passage states that the more apparent (azhar) and later relied-upon (mu'tamad) view is acceptance.
The ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi, not inter-madhhab.
3
Grasp the Reasoning (Talil)
The key rationale is that the connection is not 'lazim' (necessary). For example, having a child in a maktab does not make the parent a direct beneficiary; the benefit is incidental. Similarly, a faqih teaching at a madrasa does not have a vested interest that guarantees bias.
Absence of direct, necessary interest weakens the tuhma.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The passage concludes with 'al-mu'tamad al-qabul fi al-kull' — the relied-upon view is acceptance in all cases. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
This is based on later Hanafi authorities like al-Bazzaziyya and al-Zahiriyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقي من جنس المسائل السابقة مسألة لو شهدا على وقف في مكتب فيه أولادهم قيل يصح، وقيل لا والأظهر الصحة لأن كون أولادهم في المكتب غير لازم فلا تكون شهادتهم لهم كشهادة أهل المدرسة وفي وقف الظهيرية بعد أن ذكر مسألة المدرسة وشهادة أهلها وشهادة أهل المحلة في وقف على المحلة ما نصه وكذلك الشهادة على وقف مكتب وللشاهد صبي في المكتب لا تقبل قيل وفي هذ المسائل كلها تقبل وهو الصحيح ا هـ . القبول في البزازية في مسألة المكتب وشهادة أهل المحلة في وقف المسجد صححه وهكذا ا هـ . وشهادة الفقهاء على وقفية وقف على مدرسة كذا وهم من أهل تلك المدرسة والشهادة على وقف المسجد الجامع، وكذا أبناء السبيل إذا شهدوا بوقف على أبناء السبيل إلى آخره، فالمعتمد القبول في الكل.
There remains from the category of the previous issues the case: if two testify about a waqf for a maktab in which their children are, it is said to be valid, and it is said not; the most apparent is validity, because their children being in the maktab is not necessary, so their testimony is not like the testimony of the people of the madrasa. And in the waqf of al-Zahiriyya, after he mentioned the issue of the madrasa and the testimony of its people, and the testimony of the people of the neighborhood in a waqf for the neighborhood, his text: 'Likewise, testimony regarding a waqf for a maktab while the witness has a child in that maktab is not accepted; it is said that in all these cases it is accepted and that is the correct view.' Acceptance in al-Bazzaziyya regarding the maktab issue and the testimony of the people of the neighborhood in a waqf for the masjid is considered sahih. And testimony of the fuqaha regarding the waqf of a madrasa while they are among the people of that madrasa, and testimony regarding the waqf of a congregational mosque, and likewise wayfarers if they testify about a waqf for wayfarers, etc. So the relied-upon view is acceptance in all cases.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings on the testimony of individuals who have some connection to a waqf. The issue is whether such witnesses are suspect of partiality (tuhma). The author discusses several scenarios: (1) parents testifying about a waqf for a school where their children study; (2) fuqaha testifying about a waqf for their own madrasa; (3) residents of a neighborhood testifying about a waqf for that neighborhood; (4) wayfarers testifying about a waqf for wayfarers. In each case, there is a difference of opinion, but the author states that the relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad) is acceptance of their testimony. The reasoning is that their connection is not so immediate that it creates a presumption of partiality. The outcome of this ruling is that judges may accept such testimony unless actual suspicion arises.

Key Terms
التهمة (al-tuhma): Suspicion of partiality that disqualifies a witness in cases where they have a personal interest.
لازم (lazim): Necessary or binding; in this context, a connection that is indispensable to the witness's interest.
المعتمد (al-mu'tamad): The relied-upon or authoritative position within the school, especially in later fatwa practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in this passage, what is the ruling on testimony of a faqih about a waqf for the madrasa where he is a teacher?
A) Not accepted due to personal interest.
B) Accepted only if he has no salary from the waqf.
C) Accepted, because the connection is not deemed to cause suspicion.
D) Accepted only for the original endowment, not for revenue matters.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that testimony of persons with incidental connections to a waqf is accepted unless actual bias is proven.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony of the Nadhir on Waqf: Asl vs Ghalla
Ruling with proof through qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when the testimony of a waqf nadhir is accepted (maqbul) versus rejected (ghayr maqbul) and explain the legal reasoning (qiyas to partner testimony).

Core Idea
A nadhir's testimony on the waqf's origin is accepted; on its revenue is rejected due to personal interest.

Many assume that a waqf overseer (nadhir) cannot testify about the waqf he manages. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the nuance: he may testify about the original endowment (asl), but not about revenue matters (ghalla) because he has a direct interest, making him suspect (mutaham). The ruling is derived by analogy to partner testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of testimony
The passage distinguishes testimony regarding the 'asl al-waqf' (original endowment) and testimony regarding 'al-ghalla' (revenue/produce). Recognize that these are separate legal categories.
Asl refers to the existence and terms of the waqf; ghalla includes rents, leases, etc.
2
State the ruling for each type
The nadhir's testimony on asl is accepted (maqbul), while on ghalla it is not accepted (ghayr maqbul). Pinpoint the textual basis: 'شهادة الفقهاء بأصل الوقف' vs 'أما شهادة المستحق... لم تقبل'.
The acceptance of asl testimony is based on the general rule that fuqaha can testify on waqf.
3
Identify the underlying cause (tuhma)
The reason for rejection is 'tuhma' (suspicion). Because the nadhir has a personal right in the revenue, he is like a partner testifying for his partner. Identify the cause: having a beneficial interest creates suspicion.
Tuhma is a key concept in testimony law; it invalidates witness credibility even if the witness is honest.
4
Apply the analogy (qiyas) to partner testimony
The passage explicitly analogizes the nadhir's situation to that of a partner or joint creditor. Work through the qiyas: asl = partner testimony, far' = nadhir on ghalla, illa = shared interest, hukm = rejection.
This qiyas shows the consistency of Hanafi jurisprudence across different chapters.

وذكر ابن الشحنة بعده تنبيه ومن هذا النمط مسألة قضاء القاضي في وقف تحت نظره أو هو مستحق فيه ا هـ . قلت . تنبيه : الكلام كله في شهادة الفقهاء بأصل الوقف لقولهم شهادة الفقهاء على وقفية قوله : (ومن هذا النمط مسألة قضاء القاضي الخ قال الرملي : يعلم به جواز شهادة الناظر في وقف، أما شهادة المستحق فيما يرجع إلى الغلة كشهادته بإجارة ونحوها لم تقبل لأن له حقاً فكان متهماً فكان داخلاً في شهادة الشريك لشريكه فهو نظير شهادة أحد الدائنين لشريكه بدين مشترك بينهما، وقد كتبت في حواشي جامع الفصولين من الفصل الثالث عشر أن شهادة شهود الأوقاف المقررين في وظائف الشهادة بما يرجع إلى الغلة غير مقبولة لما ذكرنا، وكون القاضي قرره شاهداً للوقف موافقاً للشرط لا يوجب قبولها. فإن قلت : فحينئذ لا فائدة لوظيفته لأن المتولي مقبول القول في الدخل والخرج بلا بيان وقد فرض أنه لا تقبل شهادته فيما يرجع إلى الغلة قلت : فائدته إسقاط التهمة عن المتولي إذا شهد له الشاهد بالدخل والخرج فلا يحلفه القاضي إذا اتهمه ا هـ . ويقويه قولهم إن البينة تقبل لإسقاط اليمين كالمودع إذا ادعى الرد أو الهلاك فالقول له مع اليمين، فإن برهن فلا يمين، وإنما أطلنا في هذا الموضع لكثرة الاحتياج إليه في زماننا والفقه محتاج إليه كله ولا يمله أهل التحصيل.
Ibn al-Shihnah mentioned after it a note: 'From this type is the issue of the judge's ruling in a waqf under his supervision or in which he is entitled.' I say: a note: all the discussion is about testimony of the fuqaha regarding the original waqf, because they say testimony of fuqaha on waqf. His statement: 'From this type is the issue of the judge's ruling etc.' Al-Ramli said: It is learned from this the permissibility of the testimony of the nadhir regarding the waqf. As for testimony of the entitled person regarding revenue, such as his testimony about a lease and the like, it is not accepted because he has a right so he is suspect, thus it falls under the testimony of a partner for his partner. It is analogous to the testimony of one of two creditors for his partner in a joint debt. I have written in the margins of Jami' al-Fusulayn in the thirteenth chapter that the testimony of waqf witnesses appointed to the position of testimony regarding revenue matters is not accepted for what we mentioned. The fact that the judge appointed him as a witness for the waqf according to the condition does not necessitate its acceptance. If you say: Then there is no benefit to his position because the mutawalli is accepted without explanation regarding income and expenditure, and it is assumed that his testimony regarding revenue is not accepted. I say: Its benefit is to remove suspicion from the mutawalli when the witness testifies for him regarding income and expenditure, so the judge does not make him take an oath if he suspects him. This is strengthened by their statement that evidence is accepted to remove the oath, like the depositor when he claims return or destruction: his word is taken with an oath; if he brings evidence, there is no oath. We have elaborated on this point due to the great need for it in our time; fiqh is in need of it all, and the scholars do not tire of it.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage clarifies a distinction: the nadhir (overseer) of a waqf may testify about the original endowment (asl al-waqf) because he is not directly benefiting from it, but he cannot testify about matters concerning the revenue (ghalla) because he has a personal interest (he is responsible for it). This is likened to a partner testifying for his partner, which is generally not accepted due to suspicion. However, the author explains that even though the nadhir's testimony on revenue is not accepted as evidence for establishing a right, it still serves a purpose: it can remove suspicion from the mutawalli (trustee) and prevent the judge from requiring an oath. This is similar to the rule that evidence can be accepted to avert a required oath. The passage ends with the author noting the practical importance of this ruling in their time.

Key Terms
الناظر (al-nadhir): The overseer or supervisor of a waqf, responsible for its management.
الغلة (al-ghalla): The revenue or produce of the waqf property, e.g., rent from lease.
التهمة (al-tuhma): Suspicion of bias or partiality that disqualifies a witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the nadhir is not a reliable person.
B) Because the nadhir has a personal right in the revenue, making him suspect (mutaham).
C) Because the nadhir's testimony is only needed for the original waqf.
D) Because the mutawalli's statement alone is sufficient.

Key Takeaway
A waqf nadhir's testimony on the original endowment is accepted, but on revenue is rejected due to the inherent suspicion of personal interest.

Testimony of a Student or Hired Worker: When Partiality Invalidates
Ruling on testimony when dependency creates tuhma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a student for his teacher and of an exclusive hire for his employer, and distinguish between cases where tuhma invalidates testimony.

Core Idea
A witness with a strong interest in the outcome is rejected — dependency makes testimony suspect.

This lesson addresses two specific cases where testimony may be rejected due to suspicion of partiality: a student who is dependent on his teacher, and an exclusive hire who relies on his employer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between exclusive and non-exclusive hires, and the type of work matters. Understanding tuhma helps in evaluating witness credibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage discusses testimony of a student (tilmidh) for his teacher and of a hired worker (ajir) for his employer. Note the subcategories.
Student is defined as one whose harm is the teacher's harm.
2
State the ruling for each
Student's testimony for teacher: not accepted. Exclusive hire (ajir khas): not accepted. Non-exclusive hire: accepted if no tuhma.
Exclusive hire means he works specifically for that person, like a full-time servant.
3
Understand the reasoning
The basis is tuhma — suspicion of partiality due to dependency and self-interest. The student or exclusive hire may lie or exaggerate to benefit the teacher/employer.
Tuhma is a key concept in Hanafi testimony rules.
4
Apply the distinction from al-Muhit
Example: a builder hired to construct a house can testify for the owner about the house; a demolition worker hired to tear it down cannot. The builder's testimony is about his own work (no apparent bias), while the demolition worker's motive is suspect.
Task-specific hires may not create the same level of dependency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المؤلف شهادة الأجير والتلميذ وحاصل ما ذكره شارحو الهداية أن شهادة التلميذ لأستاذه لا تقبل، وفسروه بمن يعد ضرر أستاذه ضرره ونفعه نفعه، وفسره في الخلاصة بالذي يأكل مع عياله في بيته وليس له أجرة خاصة، وأما الأجير فإن كان خاصاً لم تقبل وإلا قبلت وفي المحيط : ادعى داراً فشهد له من استأجره للبناء تقبل ولو شهد له بها من استأجره لهدمها لا ا هـ .
The author did not mention the testimony of the hired worker and the student. The gist of what the commentators of al-Hidayah mentioned is that the testimony of a student for his teacher is not accepted. They interpreted it as one who considers the harm of his teacher as his harm and his benefit as his benefit. In al-Khulasa, it is interpreted as one who eats with his family in his house and has no specific wage. As for the hired worker: if he is a specific (exclusive) hire, his testimony is not accepted; otherwise it is accepted. In al-Muhit: If someone claims a house and the person he hired for building testifies for him, it is accepted; but if the person he hired for demolishing testifies for him, it is not accepted.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on two categories of witnesses with close ties to a party: (1) a student (tilmidh) who lives with or is dependent on his teacher; (2) a hired worker (ajir). For the student, if his interests are aligned with the teacher's to the extent that he considers the teacher's gain as his own, his testimony is rejected. For the hired worker, the key distinction is whether the hire is 'khas' (exclusive/specific) or not. An exclusive hire (like a full-time servant) is not accepted, but a general hire (like a day labourer on a specific task) may be accepted, depending on the nature of the task. The example from al-Muhit illustrates: a builder hired to construct can testify for the owner about the house, but a demolition worker cannot, because the builder's testimony is about what he built (no apparent partiality), while the demolition worker's testimony might be suspect.

Key Terms
الأجير الخاص (al-ajir al-khas): An exclusive hired worker, one who is employed full-time or specifically for a person, as opposed to a general hire for a specific task.
التلميذ (al-tilmidh): A student who is closely dependent on his teacher, to the extent that the teacher's harm is his harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the testimony of a person hired specifically to build a house, if he testifies in favor of the owner regarding that house?
A) Not accepted, because he is an ajir.
B) Accepted, because his hire is for a specific task and not exclusive.
C) Not accepted, because he has a financial interest.
D) Accepted only if the owner also hires him for other tasks.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects testimony from individuals whose dependency on a party creates a reasonable suspicion of bias.

Testimony of a Creditor for His Debtor
Ruling on creditor testimony with conditions and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a creditor's testimony for his debtor and explain how the debtor's status (alive/bankrupt/deceased) affects admissibility.

Core Idea
A creditor may testify for his living debtor unless the debtor is bankrupt; after death, it is always rejected.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from al-Hidayah regarding when a creditor can testify in favor of his debtor. The key distinction is the debtor's financial and legal status: alive and solvent, alive and bankrupt, or deceased. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the Hanafi school balances legal testimony with potential bias (tuhma).

Guided Path
1
State the default rule
According to al-Hidayah, the testimony of a creditor for his debtor is accepted (maqbul) as long as the debtor is not bankrupt. Identify this as the foundational position.
This applies during the debtor's lifetime.
2
Identify the condition for acceptance
The condition is that the debtor must be alive and not bankrupt (muflis). If the debtor is bankrupt, there is disagreement.
Bankruptcy means debts exceed assets and assets are under judicial restriction.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute when bankrupt
If the debtor is bankrupt, al-Muhit rejects the testimony, while Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani accepts it. Note that the passage does not resolve this disagreement.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Identify the unanimous ruling after death
If the debtor dies, the testimony is rejected unanimously (qawlan wahidan). The reason is that the creditor's right attaches to the estate, creating a clear conflict of interest.
After death, the creditor is like a partner in the estate.
5
Understand the underlying principle (tuhma)
The ruling is based on the principle of tuhma (suspicion of partiality). Where tuhma is strong (bankrupt or deceased), testimony is rejected; where it is weak (alive and solvent), it is accepted.
Tuhma is a key concept in Hanafi testimony law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر شهادة الدائن لمديونه وفي الهداية أنها مقبولة وإن كان له دين على المديون إذا لم يكن مفلساً، واختلف فيما إذا شهد له في حال كونه مفلساً ففي المحيط : لا تقبل. وشمس الأئمة الحلواني والد صاحب المحيط قال : تقبل. وأما إذا شهد له بعد الموت فلا تقبل قولاً واحداً لتعلق حقه بالتركة
And he did not mention the testimony of the creditor for his debtor. In al-Hidayah, it is stated that it is accepted even if he has a debt from the debtor, as long as the debtor is not bankrupt. There is disagreement if he testifies for him while he is bankrupt: in al-Muhit, it is not accepted. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, the father of the author of al-Muhit, said: it is accepted. As for testifying for him after death, it is not accepted unanimously, because his right is attached to the estate.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage discusses the admissibility of testimony from a creditor in favor of his debtor. The default ruling from al-Hidayah is that such testimony is accepted during the debtor's lifetime, provided the debtor is not bankrupt (muflis). If the debtor is bankrupt, there is a disagreement: the author of al-Muhit rejects it, while Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani accepts it. However, if the debtor has died, the testimony is unanimously rejected because the creditor now has a claim against the estate, creating a direct conflict of interest. The ruling is based on the principle that where there is a clear tuhma (suspicion of partiality), testimony is rejected. During life, the creditor's right is not directly affected by the outcome (unless the debtor is bankrupt), so it is accepted; after death, the creditor's right is in the estate, so he is like a partner, and his testimony is not accepted.

Key Terms
المفلس (al-muflis): A bankrupt person whose debts exceed assets and whose assets are under judicial restriction.
شهادة الدائن لمديونه (shahadat al-dayin li-madyunihi): Testimony of a creditor in favor of his debtor in a legal proceeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is the testimony of a creditor for his debtor unanimously rejected?
A) When the debtor is alive and bankrupt.
B) When the debtor is alive and not bankrupt.
C) When the debtor has died.
D) Always, because the creditor has a personal interest.

Key Takeaway
The admissibility of a creditor's testimony for his debtor depends on the debtor's status: accepted if alive and solvent, disputed if bankrupt, rejected if deceased.

Testimony of Subordinates in Corrupt Times
Ruling on testimony of subjects for rulers in corrupt times.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a subordinate for a superior in times of corruption and identify the reasons (tuhma and fasad al-zaman).

Core Idea
Testimony of peasants for landlords is rejected when widespread corruption makes partiality inevitable.

This lesson examines a critical refinement in Hanafi fiqh concerning testimony in contexts of power imbalance and moral decay. While testimony is normally accepted from upright witnesses, pervasive corruption (fasad al-zaman) creates an overwhelming presumption of partiality (tuhma). The passage traces the evolution of this ruling from early acceptance to later rejection, as recorded in later Hanafi fatwa works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the testimony (shahada) of subjects (ra'iyya) for their superiors such as rulers, landlords, and tax collectors. The ruling is that it is not permissible (ghayr ja'iz) to accept such testimony.
The ruling applies specifically in contexts where the superior has authority over the subordinate, creating a potential for partiality.
2
Understand the basis for rejection
The rejection is based on tuhma (suspicion of partiality) due to fear or hope of favor, exacerbated by fasad al-zaman (corruption of the times). Even if the witness appears upright, the contextual corruption makes bias highly likely.
Tuhma is a preventer (mani') that overrides the apparent 'adala of the witness.
3
Trace the scholarly development
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Najm al-A'imma initially accepted the testimony, then retracted. Sharaf al-A'imma and Ibn al-Shihnah explicitly rejected it. This shows the ruling emerged from later reflection on changing social conditions.
The development demonstrates how fatawa can shift with context while remaining within the Hanafi usul framework.
4
Apply to analogous situations
The passage extends the ruling beyond the original example: peasants for village chief, subjects for ruler or tax collector, and anyone with authority over the witness. The key is the power dynamic and corruption.
The examples given are illustrative, not exhaustive.
5
Note the authoritative weight
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq declares this the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) for his time, which becomes the operative fatwa. This is a fatawa mutakhkhirin ruling, not from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The authority_weight affects how binding the ruling is in fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ابن الشحنة في شرح الوهبانية : وعنه من يتكلم في أحاديث الرعية وقسم النوائب والضرائب لا تقبل شهادته. وكتب بعض الأفاضل أي شهادة الرعية له للتهمة ثم قال عنه يعني نجم الأئمة : تقبل شهادة المزارع لرب الأرض ثم رجع وقال : لا تقبل لفساد الزمان. وعن شرف الأئمة الأسفيدري : لا تقبل شهادة الرعية لوكيل الرعية والشحنة والريس والعامل الجهلهم وميلهم خوفاً منه وكذا شهادة المزارع اهـ. فهو صريح في عدم جواز شهادة من ذكر للتهمة وفساد الزمان وهذا الذي يجب أن يعول عليه في زماننا فتدبر، وبه يعلم أن شهادة الفلاحين لشيخ قريتهم وشهادتهم للقسام الذي يقسم عليهم وشهادة الرعية الحاكمهم وعاملهم ومن له نوع ولاية عليهم لا تجوز
Ibn al-Shihnah said in Sharh al-Wahbaniyya: 'From him: whoever speaks about the affairs of the subjects and the distribution of calamities and taxes, his testimony is not accepted.' And some virtuous scholars wrote: 'The testimony of the subjects for him due to suspicion,' then he said about him, meaning Najm al-A'imma: 'The testimony of a farmer for the landowner is accepted,' then he retracted and said: 'It is not accepted due to the corruption of the times.' And from Sharaf al-A'imma al-Asfidari: 'The testimony of the subjects for the agent of the subjects, the shihna, the chief, and the tax collector is not accepted due to their ignorance and inclination out of fear from him, and likewise the testimony of the farmer.' This is explicit in the impermissibility of the testimony of those mentioned due to suspicion and corruption of the times, and this is what must be relied upon in our time. So consider. And from this it is known that the testimony of peasants for the chief of their village, and their testimony for the divider who divides among them, and the testimony of subjects for their ruler, their tax collector, and anyone who has some authority over them, is not permissible.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage addresses testimony in contexts where there is a power dynamic and potential fear or influence. In times of corruption (fasad al-zaman), scholars have ruled that the testimony of inferiors for their superiors is not accepted because of overwhelming suspicion (tuhma). The passage quotes Ibn al-Shihnah, Najm al-A'imma (who initially accepted but then retracted), and Sharaf al-A'imma, all agreeing on non-acceptance. The examples include: subjects testifying for their ruler or tax collector, peasants for their village chief, and farmers for the landowner. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq endorses this as the position to be relied upon in his own time. This ruling is a practical application of the principle that testimony is rejected when there is a risk of partiality due to fear or hope of favor.

Key Terms
فساد الزمان (fasad al-zaman): Corruption of the times, referring to widespread moral decay and fear that makes people susceptible to influence and partiality.
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion or presumption of partiality, bias, or untruthfulness due to a relationship or interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the farmer is ignorant.
B) Because the landowner will reward him.
C) Because of the corruption of the times (fasad al-zaman).
D) Because the farmer has a financial interest.

Key Takeaway
In times of corruption, Hanafi muftis rule that testimony of subordinates for superiors is not accepted due to overwhelming presumption of partiality.

Testimony of the Mukhannath, Singer, Wailer, and Enemy
Rulings on testimony of those with sinful characteristics or enmity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of a mukhannath, a female singer, a wailing woman, and a worldly enemy, and identify the conditions that accept or reject their testimony.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected for fisq or worldly enmity, but natural effeminacy or wailing over one's own calamity is accepted.

In this lesson, we examine four categories of people whose testimony may be questioned due to their conduct or relationships. The Hanafi school distinguishes between those whose actions constitute fisq (immorality) and those who merely have natural traits. The key is whether the person has committed a prohibited act or harbors sinful bias.

Guided Path
1
Identify each category and the default ruling
The passage lists four types: mukhannath, female singer (mug'hanniyah), wailing woman (na'ihah), and enemy. For each, the default ruling is that their testimony is rejected unless a specific exception applies.
Default rejection is due to fisq (immorality) or bias.
2
Distinguish between natural and acquired traits for the mukhannath
The mukhannath is defined in two ways: one who naturally has soft speech and languid limbs (testimony accepted) and one who deliberately imitates women or engages in sodomy (testimony rejected). The exception is for natural, not acquired, effeminacy.
The distinction comes from al-Hidayah and al-Mughrib.
3
Analyze the exception for the wailing woman
A wailing woman (na'ihah) who wails professionally over others' dead commits a forbidden act (haram) and her testimony is rejected. However, if she wails over her own calamity, it is not sinful, so her testimony is accepted in that context.
The hadith prohibiting 'the two foolish sounds' (al-sawtayn al-ahmaqayn) includes the wailing woman and the female singer.
4
Define worldly enmity and its effect
Enmity for worldly reasons (e.g., property, money) is sinful and creates bias, so the testimony of such an enemy is rejected. The passage implies that enmity for religious reasons might not have the same effect, though this is not elaborated.
Worldly enmity is a form of fisq because it involves sinful hatred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمخنث والمغنية والنائحة والعدوّ إن كانت عداوة دنيوية. قوله: (والمخنث) أي لا تقبل شهادته ومراده المخنث في الرديء من الأفعال لأنه قوله: (والمخنث) أي لا تقبل شهادته ومراده المخنث في الرديء من الأفعال، فأما الذي في كلامه لين وفي أعضائه تكسر فهو مقبول الشهادة؛ كذا في الهداية. وفي المغرب: المخنث في عرف الناس هو الذي يباشر الرديء من الأفعال أي أفعال النساء من التزين بزينتهن والتشبه بهن في الفعل والقول فالفعل مثل كونه محلاً للواطة، والقوا مثل تلیین کلامه باختياره تشبيهاً بالنساء ؛ كذا في البناية. وفي فتح القدير من أبواب الإمامة : المخنث بكسر النون وفتحها فإن كان الأول فهو بمعنى المتسكر في أعضائه المتلين في كلامه تشبيهاً بالنساء، وإن كان الثاني فهو الذي يعمل به لواطة ا هـ قوله : (والمغنية والنائحة) لارتكابهما محرماً لنهيه عليه الصلاة والسلام عن الصوتين الأحمقين النائحة والمغنية أي صوت النائحة والمغنية ووصف الصوت بصوت صاحبه. أطلق المغنية فشمل ما إذا كانت تغني وحدها لأن رفع صوتها حرام بخلاف الرجل، قيده بأن يغني للناس. وأطلق النائحة وهي مقيدة بالتي تنوح في مصيبة غيرها لارتكابها الحرام طمعاً في المال فتقبل شهادة النائحة في مصيبتها. وفي القاموس : ناح الرجل بكى واستبكى غيره قوله : (والمعدوان كانت عداوة دنيوية) أي لم تقبل شهادة العدو لأجل الدنيا لأن المعاداة لأجلها حرام فمن ارتكبها لا يؤمن
And the effeminate man, the female singer, the wailing woman, and the enemy if the enmity is worldly. His statement: (And the effeminate man) meaning his testimony is not accepted, and he means the effeminate man in base actions. As for the one in whose speech there is softness and in whose limbs there is weakness, his testimony is accepted; thus in al-Hidayah. And in al-Mughrib: The effeminate man in common usage is the one who engages in base actions, meaning the actions of women: adorning himself with their adornments and imitating them in action and speech. Action such as being a place for sodomy, and speech such as softening his speech voluntarily in imitation of women; thus in al-Binayah. And in Fath al-Qadir, from the chapters on Imamate: Al-mukhannath, with kasra on the nun and fatha; if the former, it means the one who is languid in limbs and soft in speech in imitation of women; if the latter, it is the one who practices sodomy. End quote. His statement: (And the female singer and the wailing woman) because they commit a forbidden act, due to his (peace be upon him) prohibition of the two foolish sounds: the wailing woman and the female singer, i.e., the sound of the wailing woman and the female singer. And he described the sound by its owner. He used the female singer absolutely, including if she sings alone, because raising her voice is forbidden, unlike a man, who is restricted to singing for people. And he used the wailing woman absolutely, but she is restricted to the one who wails over a calamity of others, because she commits a forbidden act in pursuit of wealth. So the testimony of a wailing woman regarding her own calamity is accepted. And in al-Qamus: Naha: the man wept and made others weep. His statement: (And the enemy if the enmity is worldly) meaning the testimony of an enemy is not accepted for worldly matters, because enmity for worldly reasons is forbidden, and whoever commits it is not safe.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings on testimony of four types of people: the mukhannath (effeminate man), the female singer (mug'hanniyah), the wailing woman (na'ihah), and the enemy (aduw). For the mukhannath, a distinction is made: if he engages in base, immoral actions (like sodomy or deliberate imitation of women), his testimony is rejected due to fisq. But if he merely has natural effeminacy in speech or physique, his testimony is accepted. For the female singer, testimony is rejected because singing is forbidden for women, especially raising the voice, even if alone. For the wailing woman, wailing over the dead is forbidden, but if she wails over her own calamity, her testimony is accepted. For the enemy, testimony is rejected if the enmity is for worldly reasons (e.g., property disputes), because such enmity is sinful and leads to bias. The passage relies on a hadith prohibiting 'the two foolish sounds' and on the principle that fisq (immorality) makes testimony invalid.

Key Terms
مخنث (mukhannath): An effeminate man who engages in base, immoral actions (like sodomy or deliberate imitation of women); natural effeminacy is excluded.
نائحة (na'ihah): A woman who wails professionally over a deceased person for money; her testimony is rejected except over her own calamity.
عداوة دنيوية (adawah dunyawiyyah): Worldly enmity, e.g., over property or personal disputes, which is sinful and invalidates testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which person's testimony is always rejected?
A) A woman who wails over her own child's death
B) A man who softens his speech naturally
C) A man who engages in sodomy
D) A woman who sings alone for her husband

Key Takeaway
Testimony is invalidated by fisq (immorality) or worldly enmity, with exceptions for natural traits and personal calamity.
